Commentary
This passage presents five distinct proofs against the third division—the hypothesis that God is finite from all sides. The author systematically refutes each one. Proof One argues that a finite being could have been larger or smaller, so its actual size requires a cause that particularizes it, making it dependent on a free agent—impossible for God. Proof Two shows that finitude implies having halves that are different and, due to the uniformity of nature, each half must touch the other on both faces, leading to separability and composition—impossible. Proof Three states that if God is finite, there could be empty space above Him, and if God creates another world there, that world would be above God, which is absurd. Proof Four says that if finite, God could create bodies attached to His essence from all sides, making Him subject to conjunction and separation—indicating origination. Proof Five argues that if finitude, composition, and motion are allowed in God, then we cannot deny divinity to celestial bodies like the sun and moon, as they share these attributes; this leads to absurd polytheism. The passage concludes that since all possible divisions (finite from one side, both sides, or all sides) have been proven false, it is impossible for God to be in place or direction.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Accepting that God has a size does not automatically make the sun or moon gods because they have other imperfections.
Correction: The proof shows that if finitude, composition, and motion are not defects in God, then they cease to be defects anywhere, removing the basis for distinguishing God from creatures.

A) To prove God's existence
B) To deny divinity to the sun and moon
C) To attribute creation to God
D) To believe in the Throne

Key Takeaway
The fifth proof uses a slippery slope to show that allowing any finitude in God collapses the distinction between Creator and creation, proving that God must be beyond space and direction.

In what subtle ways have you compared Allah to His creation in your heart—like assuming He feels emotions exactly as humans do—and what will you do to purify that belief?
?
The proof shows that compromising even slightly on God's transcendence opens the door to shirk. Is there any area of your life where you act as if Allah is limited—like not trusting His provision, fearing human judgment more than His, or thinking He is 'too busy' for your small problems? What step will you take today to affirm His absolute sovereignty and transcendence?

Divine Transcendence

The Third Argument: Finitude Implies a World Above God
Presents the third argument against divine spatiality: empty space above leads to a world above God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that God cannot be spatially finite because it would allow a world above Him.

Core Idea
Spatial finitude of God leads to an absurd hierarchy.

This lesson presents the third argument from Al-Matalib al-Aliyah against the idea that God occupies space. The argument uses a reductio ad absurdum: assuming God is finite in space leads to the possibility of a world above Him, which is impossible. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the logical chain: if finite from all sides → finite above → empty space above → possible creation → world above God.
The argument assumes God is in space for the sake of refutation.
2
Identify the absurd consequence
The argument concludes that it would be impossible for God to be below another world. Why is that absurd? Because God is the Highest, and nothing can be above Him.
3
Reflect on the theological implication
This argument shows that God cannot be in space at all. It reinforces the doctrine of divine transcendence (tanzih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : إنه إذا كان متناهيا من كل الجوانب ، فحينئذ يكون متناهيا من جهة فوق ، وحينئذ تكون الأحياز الفارغة حاصلة فوقه. فإذا خلق الله في تلك الأحياز الفارغة عالما آخر ، فحينئذ يلزم وقوع ذلك العالم فوق الباري ، ووقوع الباري تحت العالم . وذلك محال بالاتفاق
The third: If He is finite from all sides, then He is finite from the direction above, and then empty spaces are above Him. So if God creates another world in those empty spaces, then it would follow that that world is above the Creator, and the Creator is under the world. And that is impossible by consensus.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is an argument (reductio ad absurdum) against the claim that God exists in space. It assumes for the sake of argument that God is finite and spatially located. If so, there would be empty space above Him. God, being omnipotent, could create another world in that empty space. That world would then be above God, and God would be underneath it. This is absurd because God is the Highest, and nothing can be above Him. Therefore, the premise that God is in space is false.

Key Terms
التناهي
الجهة
الحيز
الباري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Spatial location does not imply a hierarchy of place.
Correction: The argument shows that if God is in space, then there can be empty space above Him, allowing a created world to be above God, which is absurd because God is the Highest.

Checkpoint
What does the third argument conclude about God's location?
A) He is finite.
B) He is above the world.
C) He cannot be in space.
D) He is infinite in size.

Key Takeaway
The third argument demonstrates that God cannot be spatially finite because it would allow a world above Him, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever catch yourself subconsciously imagining God as being 'somewhere'—like in the sky or above the clouds? How does this argument challenge that mental picture, and what would it mean for you to truly believe that He is beyond all space?
?
If nothing can ever be above God, what does that imply about your own status before Him? Are there areas of your life where you act as if something—money, status, your own desires—is 'above' God in your priorities? What one concrete change would show that you truly believe He is above everything?

The Fourth Argument: Spatiality Implies Composition and Contingency
Presents the fourth argument: finitude allows bodily attachment, implying composition and temporality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why spatial finiteness would imply composition and temporality for God, and how this argument supports divine transcendence.

Core Idea
If God were in space, He could be composed—making Him contingent, not divine.

The fourth argument against God being in space builds on the idea of finitude. If God has spatial boundaries, it becomes possible for Him to be attached to other things, which would make Him composite and subject to separation. Both are signs of contingency and temporality, which cannot apply to the eternal Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to see its logical flow. Then read the literal translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if finite... then...'.
The argument is concise; each phrase carries a step.
2
Identify the logical chain
Break down the argument: finitude → possible attachment → possible composition/separation → indicates temporality. Understand why composition and separation are signs of contingency.
Composition requires parts, and parts can be separated—both impossible for a necessary being.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: If God were composite, would He be dependent on His parts? How does that contradict necessary existence? This shows why God cannot be in space.
This connects to the broader theme of divine transcendence (tanzih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : إنه إذا كان متناهيا من كل الجوانب ، فحينئذ يصح من الله تعالى أن يخلق أجساما متصلة بتلك الذات من كل الجوانب ، وحينئذ يصح عليه الاجتماع والافتراق . وذلك يدل على الحدوث
The fourth: If He is finite from all sides, then it is possible for God (exalted) to create bodies connected to that essence from all sides, and then composition and separation would be possible for Him. And that indicates temporality (ḥudūth).
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is another argument against God being in space. If God were finite and located, He would have boundaries. It would then be possible for God to create bodies attached to His essence on all sides. This would result in God being composed of parts (composition) and capable of separation (being divided). Both composition and the possibility of separation are characteristics of contingent, temporal beings. Since God is necessarily eternal and not contingent, He cannot be in space.

Key Terms
الاجتماع
الافتراق
الحدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Composition in itself is not a problem for God; it is merely a structural feature.
Correction: In Islamic theology, composition implies dependency on parts and the possibility of separation, both of which are signs of contingency and temporality. Since God is necessary and eternal, He cannot be composite.

Checkpoint
Why does the fourth argument conclude that God is not in space?
A) Because bodies are evil.
B) Because it would allow God to be attached to other bodies, implying composition and contingency.
C) Because God cannot create bodies.
D) Because space is empty.

Key Takeaway
If God were in space, He would be subject to composition and separation—marks of contingency—so the eternal, necessary Creator cannot be spatial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever imagine God as located in a specific place, like a throne in the sky? How does this argument challenge that image, and what does it demand of your understanding of God's transcendence?
?
If you truly believe God is beyond space and time, does your daily worship reflect that belief, or do you still act as if He is confined to a building or direction?
?
This argument shows that spatiality implies contingency. How does this truth affect the way you seek closeness to a God who is not limited by location?

The Fifth Argument: Finite Beings Cannot Be Gods
Fifth argument: reductio against divine spatiality with objection and answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God cannot be in space or direction, and how the objection regarding God's infinity is answered by distinguishing two types of infinity.

Core Idea
If a finite being could be God, then any finite thing could be a god — an absurdity.

Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents a powerful reductio ad absurdum: if we allow that a finite, spatial being can be God, we lose the ability to deny divinity to any finite object — the sun, moon, even the Throne. The objection that God's own infinity would lead to similar problems is deflected by clarifying two distinct meanings of 'infinite.' This argument is central to establishing divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the argument's flow.
Pay attention to the three defects listed: finitude, composition, motion.
2
Understand the reductio
Notice how Razi argues: if we permit a finite, located being as God, then we cannot exclude any other finite being from divinity. This leads to absurdity, so the premise must be false.
The conclusion: God cannot be in space or direction.
3
Analyze the objection and answer
The objector says: 'You claim God is infinite, so the same problems apply.' Razi's answer distinguishes two meanings of 'infinite': one of transcendence and one of extension. God's infinity is the first kind.
This distinction preserves divine transcendence without attributing physical infinity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس : إنا إذا جوزنا في الشيء الذي يكون محدودا متناهيا من كل الجوانب : أن يكون إلها لهذا العالم ، فحينئذ لا يمكننا البتة أن نقطع بأن الشمس والقمر ليسا إلهين لهذا العالم ، لأنه لا عيب فيهما إلا أحد أمور ثلاثة : أحدهما : التناهي . والثاني : كونه مركبا من الأجزاء والأبعاض . والثالث : كونه قابلا للحركة والسكون ، فإذا جوزنا هذه الثلاثة في حق الإله تعالى فحينئذ لا يمكننا جعل هذه الأشياء عينا في الإلهية. وحينئذ لا يمكننا القدح في إلهية الشمس والقمر وسائر الكواكب . بل على هذا التقدير ، فلعل إله العالم هو العرش نفسه ، من غير حاجة إلى إثبات شيء آخر ، معلوم إن كل ما يلزم منه هذا القول ، فهو باطل بإجماع من العقلاء. فيثبت بما ذكرنا : أن إله العالم لو كان حاصلا في الجهة والحيز ، لوجب وقوعه على أحد هذه الأقسام وثبت بالدليل فسادها بأسرها ، فوجب القطع بأنه يمتنع كون الإله عز وجل حاصلا في الحيز والجهة . فإن قيل : ألستم تقولون : إنه تعالى غير متناه في ذاته فيلزمكم جميع ما ألزمتموه علينا ؟ قلنا : الشيء يقال له إنه غير متناه على وجهين أحدهما : أنه منزه عن المقدار والحجمية ، والحيز والجهة . ومتى كان الأمر كذلك ، امتنع أن يكون لذاته حد ومقطع ونهاية. والثاني : أن يكون في ذاته حجما ومقدارا ، إلا أنه ممتدا امتدادا بغير النهاية ، بمعنى أنه لا ينتهي إلى حد ومقطع ، إلا وتجد بعد ذلك منه شيئا آخر . فإذا قلنا : إن ذات الله تعالى غير متناهية : عنينا به الأول . لا الثاني وعلى هذا التقسيم، فالتفسير الذي ذكرناه في إبطال قولكم غير وارد علينا .
The fifth: If we allow that a thing which is limited and finite from all sides can be a god for this world, then we can never be certain that the sun and moon are not gods for this world, because there is no defect in them except three matters: first, finitude; second, being composed of parts and limbs; third, being subject to motion and rest. So if we allow these three for the divine, then we cannot make these things defective for divinity. And then we cannot impugn the divinity of the sun, moon, and other planets. Rather, on this assumption, perhaps the god of the world is the Throne itself, without need to establish anything else. It is known that every consequence of this statement is false by consensus of the rational. So it is established by what we have mentioned: that if the god of the world were in direction and space, he would necessarily fall under one of these divisions, and it is established by proof the corruption of all of them, so it is necessary to conclude that it is impossible for God (mighty and majestic) to be in space and direction. If it is said: Do you not say that He is infinite in His essence, so you are subject to all that you have imposed on us? We say: A thing is said to be infinite in two ways: one: that it is free from magnitude, volume, space, and direction. When this is the case, it is impossible for it to have a limit, cut, or end. The second: that it has size and magnitude in itself, but it extends infinitely, meaning it does not reach a limit or cut without there being something else after it. So when we say that the essence of God is infinite, we mean the first, not the second. And on this division, the explanation we gave in refuting your statement does not apply to us.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage contains the fifth argument against God being in space, followed by an objection and its answer. The argument is: if a finite, spatially located being can be God, then the sun, moon, and other finite objects could also be gods, since they share the same defects: finitude, composition, and motion. This would lead to polytheism or the absurd conclusion that the Throne itself might be God, which is rejected by consensus. Therefore, God cannot be in space. The objection claims that if God is infinite, the same arguments would apply to Him. The answer distinguishes two meanings of 'infinite': (1) free from all magnitude and location (God's infinity), and (2) extending infinitely in size (not applicable to God). Thus, the objection is refuted.

Key Terms
التناهي
التركيب
الحركة والسكون
غير متناه
الحجم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's infinity means He has an infinitely large body or extends infinitely in space.
Correction: God's infinity is a transcendence from all physical properties like magnitude and location, not an infinite extension in size.

Checkpoint
What is the two-fold distinction regarding infinity?
A) Infinite in time and space.
B) Transcendence vs. infinite extension.
C) Infinite in power and knowledge.
D) Infinite in essence and attributes.

Key Takeaway
God's transcendence requires that He is free from all spatial attributes, and His infinity means no physical limit, not infinite size.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray, do you unconsciously picture God as being above the sky? How would your connection with Him change if you truly believed He is beyond all space, not located anywhere? What is one concrete step you can take today to internalize this truth?
?
If someone said, 'If God is not in space, then He is nowhere, so He doesn't exist,' would you be able to answer them using the two meanings of infinite from this lesson? Is your own heart completely settled on this, or do you have lingering doubts?
?
The sun and moon are finite, yet some worship them. What finite 'gods'—like status, wealth, relationships, or your own desires—are you giving the devotion that only the transcendent Creator deserves? Name one right now, and commit to dethroning it today through a specific action.

The Fourth Proof: Necessity or Possibility of Spatial Location Refuted
Fourth proof: God's place would be necessary or possible; both refuted

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the fourth proof refutes God's spatiality by showing that necessity or possibility of being in a specific space leads to impossibility.

Core Idea
God's spatiality is impossible because it would require either necessary or possible occupancy, both rationally untenable.

Sanusi presents the fourth proof against God being in space. He divides the scenario into two logical possibilities: God's presence in a specific space is either necessary or possible. He then refutes the necessity branch with two arguments, establishing that spatiality cannot be attributed to God.

Guided Path
1
Understand the logical division
The proof sets up a binary: if God is in a specific space, it must be either necessary or possible. Recognise this as a rational classification.
This is a typical kalam method of dividing possibilities.
2
First argument against necessity
Examine the first argument: if one body necessarily occupies a space, all bodies equal in quiddity must also occupy that same space, leading to impossible coexistence.
The premise is that things equal in essence share all necessitated properties.
3
Second argument against necessity
The second argument: pure void has no distinguishing features, so no specific space is necessary. The text breaks off here.
Even though incomplete, the reasoning is clear: no particular direction is special.
4
Reflect on the overall proof
Consider why the possibility branch is also false. The text implies it, and the commentary explains that both are invalid.
The proof ends with the necessity branch refuted, implying the possibility branch is similarly invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : إنه تعالى لو حصل في شيء من الأحياز والجهات ، لكان إما أنه يحصل في ذلك الحيز المعين ، مع وجوب أن يحصل فيه أو مع جواز أن يحصل فيه والقسمان باطلان ، فكان القول بحصوله في الحيز باطلا أما الحصر فظاهر . وأما القسم الأول . وهو أنه يقال : حصل في ذلك الحيز . ، مع وجوب أن يحصل فيه : فهو قول باطل . ويدل عليه وجوه : الأول : إن كل ما كان حجمها ، شاغلا للحيز ، وجب أن يكون مساويا لسائر الأجسام ، ولسائر الأحجام في تمام الماهية ، على ما قررنا هذه المقدمة في الفصول السابقة . وإذا ثبت هذا ، فنقول : لو وجب حصول واحد منها في حيز معين ، لوجب حصول كلها في ذلك الحيز ، ضرورة أن الأشياء المتساوية في تمام الماهية ، يجب اشتراكها في جميع اللوازم ، وحينئذ يلزم اجتماع الذوات الكثيرة في الحيز الواحد ، وذلك محال . والثاني : وهو أن الحدود والجوانب المفترضة في الخلاء الصرف ، متشابهة ومتساوية في تمام الماهية. فإن الخلاء الصرف لا حقيقة له ولا ماهية له ، إلا
The fourth proof: If the Exalted were to be in any of the spaces and directions, then either He is in that specific space necessarily, or He could be in it possibly. Both divisions are false, so the statement of His being in space is false. As for the division (it is obvious). As for the first division, which is that He is in that space necessarily: it is a false statement. There are proofs for this: The first: Everything that has volume, occupying space, must be equal to other bodies and other volumes in the entirety of quiddity, as we established this premise in previous chapters. And if this is established, we say: If the presence of one of them in a specific space were necessary, then the presence of all of them in that space would be necessary, because things equal in the entirety of quiddity must share in all necessary concomitants. And then many essences would coexist in one space, which is impossible. The second: The limits and sides assumed in pure void are similar and equal in the entirety of quiddity. For pure void has no reality and no quiddity, except [text breaks off]
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a proof (the fourth) against God being in space. It sets up a division: if God were in a specific space, it would be either necessary (He must be there) or possible (He could be there). Both are shown false. The proof then focuses on the necessary case, offering two arguments: (1) If one body necessarily occupies a specific space, all bodies equal in quiddity (essence) must also occupy that space, leading to multiple substances in one location, which is impossible. (2) The limits of pure void are all alike, so no specific point is distinguished; thus nothing makes a particular space necessary. The text is incomplete but the reasoning is clear: spatiality cannot be necessary, and the possible case is also invalid (as implied by the overall argument).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's presence in space could be merely possible rather than necessary, avoiding the necessity argument.
Correction: The overall proof explicitly says both divisions are false. The possibility branch is also invalid, though the text focuses on necessity.

Checkpoint
What is the first argument against the necessity of God's being in a specific space?
A) All bodies must occupy different spaces.
B) If one must be in a specific space, all equal bodies must also be there, leading to impossible coexistence.
C) Space is infinite.
D) God is not a body.

Key Takeaway
The fourth proof rationally excludes any possibility of God being in space by showing that both necessity and possibility lead to absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

If God's presence is not dependent on space, then your sin does not 'distance' you from Him in a literal sense. What does it really mean to be 'far' from God? Are you using spiritual distance as an excuse to delay repentance?

The Two Meanings of 'Non-Finite' and Their Application to God
The author distinguishes two meanings of 'non-finite' and applies only one to God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two distinct meanings of 'non-finite' and why only one applies to God.

Core Idea
God is infinite in transcendence, not in size.

When we say God is 'infinite,' we must be careful about what we mean. The author responds to an objection by clarifying that 'non-finite' has two very different senses. One is about being free from physical limitations; the other is about endless extension in space. This lesson unpacks that crucial distinction, which protects divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own wording introduce the distinction.
Notice that the author begins by citing an opponent's challenge.
2
Identify the two meanings
Look for the two meanings of 'non-finite' (غير متناهي). The first is about transcendence; the second is about endless extension in space. Note the key terms: quantity, corporeality, space, direction.
The first meaning denies all physical categories; the second assumes them.
3
Apply the distinction to God
See which meaning the author applies to God. He explicitly chooses the first and rejects the second. Ask yourself why the second cannot apply to God.
This distinction blocks the opponent's objection and safeguards tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جميع ما ألزمتموه علينا ؟ قلنا : الشيء يقال له إنه غير متناهي على وجهين أحدهما : أنه منزه عن المقدار والحجمية ، والحيز والجهة . ومتى كان الأمر كذلك ، امتنع أن يكون لذاته حد ومقطع ونهاية. والثاني : أن يكون في ذاته حجها ومقدارا ، إلا أنه ممتدا امتدادا بغير النهاية ، بمعنى أنه لا ينتهي إلى حد ومقطع ، إلا وتجد بعد ذلك منه شيئا آخر . فإذا قلنا : إن ذات الله تعالى غير متناهية : عنينا به الأول . لا الثاني وعلى هذا التقسيم، فالتفسير الذي ذكرناه في إبطال قولكم غير وارد علينا .
All that you have imposed upon us? We said: A thing is said to be non-finite in two ways: one: that it is transcendent beyond quantity and corporeality, and space and direction. And when it is so, it is impossible for it to have a limit, an extremity, or an end. The second: that it has in itself size and magnitude, but it extends without end, meaning that it does not reach a limit or extremity except that you find after that another thing from it. So when we say that the essence of God Almighty is non-finite, we mean the first, not the second. And according to this division, the interpretation that we mentioned in refuting your statement does not apply to us.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage defines two meanings of 'non-finite' (غير متناهي) in response to an objection. The author begins by reporting a question: 'All that you have imposed upon us?' Then he gives the answer. The first meaning is that something is free from quantity, corporeality, space, and direction; it has no limit or end in essence. This applies to God. The second meaning is that something has size and magnitude but extends infinitely, i.e., it never reaches a final limit. This applies to created bodies like space. When the author says God is non-finite, he means the first, not the second. This distinction rescues his earlier argument from the opponent's objection.

Key Terms
غير متناهي (non-finite)
مقدار (quantity)
حجمية (corporeality)
حيز (space)
جهة (direction)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that saying 'God is infinite' means He has limitless size, like a vast body that extends forever.
Correction: The passage clarifies that God's infinity means He is beyond all physical categories—quantity, space, direction—not that He has endless extension.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does it mean to say that God is 'non-finite' (غير متناهي)?
A) He has no beginning or end in time.
B) He is transcendent beyond quantity, space, and direction.
C) He is huge and extends endlessly.
D) He has no parts or attributes.

Key Takeaway
When describing God as 'non-finite,' it means He transcends all physical limitations, not that He has infinite size.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The author distinguishes two meanings of 'non-finite'. Have you ever attributed a finite quality to God in your thoughts, such as seeing Him as limited by time or place? What is one concrete thought you will catch and reject this week?

The Fourth Proof: Necessity of Location Leads to Absurdity
Sanusi presents the fourth proof and its first sub-argument against necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the structure of the fourth proof and the first argument that if God necessarily occupied a space, all bodies would have to occupy the same space, which is absurd.

Core Idea
If God were necessarily in a place, all equal bodies would crowd into that one spot.

This lesson introduces the fourth proof against God being in space. The author frames the proof as a dilemma: if God were in a place, it would be either necessary or possible. Both are false. We focus here on the first horn—necessity—and its first refutation using the principle that all bodies share the same quiddity.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof statement
Read the opening lines of the passage in Arabic and translation to understand the dilemma: necessary or possible occurrence in a space.
Notice the author's method: a logical division (qismah) followed by refutation of each.
2
Examine the first refutation
Focus on the first aspect (al-wajh al-awwal) of refuting necessity. The author uses the premise that all bodies equal in complete quiddity must share all necessary concomitants; if one body necessarily occupies a space, all must, leading to many essences in one space—impossible.
This argument relies on earlier established premises about quiddity.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Ask yourself: How does this argument show that God cannot be necessarily located? It does so by showing necessary location leads to an impossible consequence.
The argument is indirect: it shows the consequence is false, so the premise must be false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : إنه تعالى لو حصل في شيء من الأحياز والجهات ، لكان إما أنه يحصل في ذلك الحيز المعين ، مع وجوب أن يحصل فيه [ أو مع جواز أن يحصل فيه ] والقسمان باطلان ، فكان القول بحصوله في الحيز باطلا أما الحصر فظاهر . وأما القسم الأول . وهو أنه يقال : حصل في ذلك الحيز . ، مع وجوب أن يحصل فيه : فهو قول باطل . ويدل عليه وجوه : الأول : إن كل ما كان حجمها ، شاغلا للحيز ، وجب أن يكون مساويا لسائر الأجسام ، ولسائر الأحجام في تمام الماهية ، على ما قررنا هذه المقدمة في الفصول السابقة . وإذا ثبت هذا ، فنقول : لو وجب حصول واحد منها في حيز معين ، لوجب حصول كلها في [ ذلك ] الحيز ، ضرورة أن الأشياء المتساوية في تمام الماهية ، يجب اشتراكها في جميع اللوازم ، [ وحينئذ يلزم اجتماع الذوات ] الكثيرة في الحيز الواحد ، وذلك محال . والثاني : وهو أن الحدود والجوانب المفترضة في الخلاء الصرف ، متشابهة ومتساوية في تمام الماهية. فإن الخلاء الصرف لا حقيقة له ولا ماهية له ، إلا مجرد كونه خلاء صرفا وفضاء صرفا . وإذا كانت الأجزاء المفترضة فيها تلك متشابهة ، فلو وجب حصول ذات في واحد منها ، لوجب حصولها في جميع الأحياز [ وحينئذ يلزم حصول ذات الواحد في جميع الأحياز ] دفعة واحدة . وذلك محال . فإن قالوا : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إن الأجزاء المفترضة ، يخالف بعضها بعضا ، بسبب أن بعضها فوق ، وبعضها تحت . والله تعالى يجب حصوله في الفوق ، ويمتنع حصوله في التحت ؟ فنقول : الفوق أو التحت إنما يظهر بعد خلق العالم ، فأما قبل خلق العالم ، فليس هناك فوق ولا تحت ، ولا يتميز جانب في الخلاء الذي لا نهاية له ، عن جانب آخر بشيء من الخواص والصفات البتة . [ وأيضا : أجزاء الفضاء متشابهة في كونها قضاء صرفا ، وخلاء محضا ] فنقول : لو اختلفت في شيء من الخواص والصفات ، لكان المقتضي لتلك الخاصية المعينة أما أن يكون هو نفس طبيعة الفضاء والخلاء ، فيلزم أن يكون ما به الاشتراك علة لما به الامتياز ، وذلك محال . وإما أن يكون المقتضي هو الشيء الذي يكون محلا لذلك الخلاء والفضاء وذلك أيضا محال لأنا بينا : أن طبيعة البعد والامتداد ، يمتنع أن تكون صفة قائمة بذات أخرى . وأيضا : فعلى هذا التقدير يكون الخلاء جسما لا معنى ، لأنه لا معنى للجسم إلا البعد الحال في المادة، وإما أن يكون المقتضي هو الذي يكون حالا في ذلك البعد . وحينئذ يعود التقسيم المذكور في المقتضي لذلك الأمر ، وإن كان لأمر آخر ، لزم التسلسل وهو محال . فيثبت بهذا البرهان : أنه يمتنع أن يقع الاختلاف بين أجزاء الخلاء والفضاء. وحينئذ يحصل المقصود .
والوجه الثالث في بيان أنه يمتنع كون ذات الله حاصلة في حيز معين على سبيل الوجوب : أنه لو حصل في حيز معين مع أنه يمتنع عليه أن ينتقل من ذلك الحيز إلى حيز آخر ، لزم أن يقال : إنه كالزمن المقعد ، العاجز عن
The fourth proof: If God Almighty were to occur in some space or direction, then either He would occur in that specific space with its occurrence being necessary, or with its occurrence being permissible. Both divisions are false, so the statement that He occurs in space is false. As for the restriction, it is apparent. As for the first division—that it is said: He occurred in that space, with it being necessary that He occur in it—it is a false statement. Proof of this is shown by aspects: First: Every thing that has size and occupies space must be equal to other bodies and other sizes in complete quiddity, as we have established this premise in previous chapters. Now, if it is necessary for one of them to occur in a specific space, then it would be necessary for all of them to occur in that space, because things equal in complete quiddity must share all necessary concomitants. Then this would necessitate the coming together of many essences in one space, and that is impossible. Second: The limits and sides assumed in pure void are similar and equal in complete quiddity. For pure void has no reality and no quiddity except merely being pure void and pure space. And if the assumed parts in it are similar, then if it were necessary for an essence to occur in one of them, it would be necessary for it to occur in all spaces and then this would necessitate the occurrence of a single essence in all spaces at once, and that is impossible. If they say: Why is it not permissible to say that the assumed parts differ from one another due to some being above and some being below, and God Almighty must occur in the above and cannot occur in the below? We say: Above and below only become apparent after the creation of the world. But before the creation of the world, there is no above or below, nor does a side in the infinite void become distinguished from another side by any properties or attributes at all. Moreover, if they differed in any properties or attributes, then the determinant for that specific property would either be the very nature of space and void—which would entail that the commonality is the cause of the distinction, and that is impossible—or the determinant would be the thing that is the locus of that void and space—that too is impossible, for we have shown that the nature of dimension and extension cannot be an attribute subsisting in another essence. Moreover, on this supposition, the void would become a body in meaning, because the meaning of body is nothing but dimension subsisting in matter. Or the determinant would be what is subsisting in that dimension, and then the prior division would return concerning the determinant for that matter. And if it were for another reason, infinite regress would follow, which is impossible. Thus it is established by this proof that difference cannot occur between parts of void and space, and thereby the objective is achieved. The third aspect in explaining that it is impossible for God's essence to occur in a specific space on the basis of necessity: If it occurred in a specific space while it is impossible for it to move from that space to another, then it must be said that it is like a paralyzed, incapacitated one...
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage contains the fourth proof against God being located in space or direction. The author first states the proof: if God were in a place, it would be either necessary or permissible; both are impossible. He then refutes the first division (necessary location) through three aspects. The first aspect uses the premise that all bodies are equal in quiddity; if one necessarily occupies a certain place, all would, leading to impossible coexistence. The second aspect argues that the parts of pure void are indistinguishable, so if God necessarily occupied one, He would occupy all, which is absurd. The author then addresses an objection: that the parts differ by above and below. He replies that above and below only exist after creation; before creation, the void is undifferentiated. He then gives a separate argument that any differentiation in the void would lead to an infinite regress or other absurdities. The third aspect is only partially given: if God were fixed in one place, He would be like a paralyzed person, implying deficiency. The text cuts off here, but the argument is that such immobility is incompatible with divine perfection.

Key Terms
حيز (space)
وجوب (necessity)
تمام الماهية (complete quiddity)
لازم (necessary concomitant)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are all different in quiddity.
B) They are equal in complete quiddity.
C) They necessarily occupy different spaces.
D) They can occupy the same space.

Key Takeaway
If God's location were necessary, then all bodies would have to be in the same place—impossible, so necessity is false.

?
The proof shows that assuming necessity of location leads to absurdity. In your life, do you treat your own beliefs as necessary without examining their implications? Will you commit to examining one of your beliefs about God this week using similar logical scrutiny?

Pure Void and the Illusion of Direction
Sanusi provides the second aspect of refuting necessity and addresses an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument against necessity—that pure void parts are indistinguishable, so if God were in one, He would be in all—and the refutation of the objection that directions (above/below) differentiate the void.

Core Idea
Pure void has no distinctions; if God were in one part, He'd be everywhere in the void.

This lesson continues the refutation of the necessity division. The second argument uses the nature of pure void: its parts are similar, so necessary location in one implies location in all. The author then anticipates an objection: that directions like above and below differentiate the void. He replies that such directions only exist after creation, and that any differentiation would lead to absurdities.

Guided Path
1
Read the second argument
Read the text about the limits and sides in pure void. Notice the key point: the parts of pure void are similar in quiddity.
Pure void has no intrinsic properties.
2
Follow the objection
The opponent says: But parts differ by above and below, and God must be above. The author responds: Above/below only appear after creation.
This shows the argument is about pre-creation state.
3
Understand the deeper refutation
The author then argues that any differentiation would require a cause, leading to an infinite regress or making void a body, etc.
This is a sophisticated metaphysical argument.

The fourth proof: If God Almighty were to occur in some space or direction, then either He would occur in that specific space with its occurrence being necessary, or with its occurrence being permissible. Both divisions are false, so the statement that He occurs in space is false. As for the restriction, it is apparent. As for the first division—that it is said: He occurred in that space, with it being necessary that He occur in it—it is a false statement. Proof of this is shown by aspects: First: Every thing that has size and occupies space must be equal to other bodies and other sizes in complete quiddity, as we have established this premise in previous chapters. Now, if it is necessary for one of them to occur in a specific space, then it would be necessary for all of them to occur in that space, because things equal in complete quiddity must share all necessary concomitants. Then this would necessitate the coming together of many essences in one space, and that is impossible. Second: The limits and sides assumed in pure void are similar and equal in complete quiddity. For pure void has no reality and no quiddity except merely being pure void and pure space. And if the assumed parts in it are similar, then if it were necessary for an essence to occur in one of them, it would be necessary for it to occur in all spaces and then this would necessitate the occurrence of a single essence in all spaces at once, and that is impossible. And if it were for another reason, infinite regress would follow, which is impossible. Thus it is established by this proof that difference cannot occur between parts of void and space, and thereby the objective is achieved. Impossibility of Differentiation in Void Space
The author proves that parts of void and space cannot differ, establishing a key premise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the parts of pure void and space cannot differ in any property, and how this premise is crucial for arguments about God's transcendence beyond spatial limitations.

Core Idea
All parts of pure space are identical—no property distinguishes any part.

This lesson examines a key philosophical argument for God's transcendence above spatial limitations. The author proves that before creation, the parts of void and space are indistinguishable, so God cannot be necessarily located in any particular part. This argument also rejects any claim that 'above' or 'below' are absolute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. The main claim is that the parts of pure void and space cannot differ in any property.
Notice that the author begins by stating that if the parts were similar, then if one must contain an essence, all must.
2
Understand the objection about 'above' and 'below'
An objector suggests that parts differ because some are above and some below, and God must be above. The author responds that these concepts only exist after creation; before the world, there is no distinction.
This objection is based on a common misconception that direction is intrinsic to space.
3
Examine the three-part response that eliminates all grounds for differentiation
The author then presents a rigorous argument: if parts differed, the cause of difference must be either the nature of void itself (impossible, as it is shared), a substrate for the void (impossible, as void cannot be an attribute), or an inhering accident (leads to infinite regress). All options are impossible.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum that covers all logical possibilities.
4
Connect the conclusion to the broader theme of divine transcendence
The conclusion that all parts of void are identical supports the idea that God cannot be necessarily located in any specific place, reinforcing divine transcendence.
This premise is used in later arguments about God's independence from space.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مجرد كونه خلاء صرفا وفضاء صرفا . وإذا كانت الأجزاء المفترضة فيها تلك متشابهة ، فلو وجب حصول ذات في واحد منها ، لوجب حصولها في جميع الأحياز وحينئذ يلزم حصول ذات الواحد في جميع الأحياز دفعة واحدة . وذلك محال . فإن قالوا : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إن الأجزاء المفترضة ، يخالف بعضها بعضا ، بسبب أن بعضها فوق ، وبعضها تحت . والله تعالى يجب حصوله في الفوق ، ويمتنع حصوله في التحت ؟ فنقول : الفوق أو التحت إنما يظهر بعد خلق العالم ، فأما قبل خلق العالم ، فليس هناك فوق ولا تحت ، ولا يتميز جانب في الخلاء الذي لا نهاية له ، عن جانب آخر بشيء من الخواص والصفات البتة . وأيضا : أجزاء الفضاء متشابهة في كونها قضاء صرفا ، وخلاء محضا فنقول : لو اختلفت في شيء من الخواص والصفات ، لكان المقتضي لتلك الخاصية المعينة أما أن يكون هو نفس طبيعة الفضاء والخلاء ، فيلزم أن يكون ما به الاشتراك علة لما به الامتياز ، وذلك محال . وإما أن يكون المقتضي هو الشيء الذي يكون محلا لذلك الخلاء والفضاء وذلك أيضا محال لأنا بينا : أن طبيعة البعد والامتداد ، يمتنع أن تكون صفة قائمة بذات أخرى . وأيضا : فعلى هذا التقدير يكون الخلاء جسما لا معنى ، لأنه لا معنى للجسم إلا البعد الحال في المادة، وإما أن يكون المقتضي هو الذي يكون حالا في ذلك البعد . وحينئذ يعود التقسيم المذكور في المقتضي لذلك الأمر ، وإن كان لأمر آخر ، لزم التسلسل وهو محال . فيثبت بهذا البرهان : أنه يمتنع أن يقع الاختلاف بين أجزاء الخلاء والفضاء. وحينئذ يحصل المقصود .
Merely its being pure void and pure space. And if the assumed parts in it are similar, then if the occurrence of an essence in one of them were necessary, its occurrence would be necessary in all the places, and then the occurrence of that one essence in all places at once would follow. That is impossible. If they say: Why is it not permissible to say that the assumed parts differ from each other, because some are above and some are below, and God the Most High must occur in the above and cannot occur in the below? We say: Above or below only appear after the creation of the world; as for before the creation of the world, there is no above or below, and no side in the infinite void is distinguished from another side by any properties or attributes at all. Also: The parts of space are similar in being pure vacuum and pure void; we say: if they differed in some property or attribute, then the determinant of that specific property would either be the very nature of space and void, then what is common would be the cause of what distinguishes, and that is impossible; or the determinant would be the thing that is a locus for that void and space, and that is also impossible because we have shown that the nature of dimension and extension cannot be an attribute subsisting in another essence. Also, on this assumption, the void would be a body without meaning, because body means nothing but dimension inhering in matter; or the determinant would be what inheres in that dimension, and then the division mentioned regarding the determinant of that matter recurs; and if it were for another matter, infinite regress would follow, which is impossible. By this proof it is established that it is impossible for differences to occur among the parts of void and space; and then the intended point is obtained.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents a proof that the parts of pure void and space are identical and cannot differ. The author begins by stating that if the void and space are pure (i.e., not qualified by any property), then its hypothetical parts are similar. If it were necessary for an essence (i.e., God) to occur in one part, it would be necessary in all, which is impossible. An objector then suggests that parts differ by being above or below, and God must be above. The author answers that above and below only arise after creation; before the world, there is no distinction. The author then strengthens the argument: if parts did differ, the cause of the difference would either be the nature of void itself (which is shared, so it cannot be a cause of difference), or a substrate for the void (but void cannot be an attribute of a substance), or an inherence in the void (which leads to a regress). All alternatives are impossible, thus proving that parts of void and space cannot differ. This conclusion is a premise for showing that God cannot be necessarily in a specific place, because all places are equivalent.

الوجوب (al-wujub)

التسلسل (al-tasalsul)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume that 'above' and 'below' are intrinsic, absolute directions in space, even before creation.
Correction: The author clarifies that above and below only appear after the creation of the world; before creation, there is no distinction.

Key Takeaway
The parts of pure void and space are essentially identical, so God cannot be necessarily bound to any spatial location.

Third Proof: Localization Necessitates Impotence
A proof that necessary localization implies impotence via analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why necessary localization in a specific place would imply impotence, and why that is impossible for Allah.

Core Idea
If Allah were stuck in one place, He would be like a paralyzed man—utterly deficient.

This third proof uses a vivid analogy to expose the absurdity of saying Allah is necessarily confined to a specific location. The author argues that such a state would render Allah immobile and powerless, like a crippled old man—a description utterly incompatible with divine perfection. As you read, notice how the analogy drives home the point that necessary localization entails deficiency.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own reasoning come through.
2
Identify the key components
Break down the argument: the condition (necessary localization), the impossibility of movement, the analogy of the crippled old man, and the conclusion that such a state is deficient and Allah is above it.
3
Reflect on the analogy
Ask yourself why the author chose a crippled old man as an analogy. What emotional and rational force does it carry? How does it highlight the absurdity of the opposing view?
4
Connect to the broader doctrine
Consider how this proof fits into the larger argument for Allah's transcendence (tanzih) and against anthropomorphism.
This proof shows that necessary localization would confine Allah, contradicting His absolute power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثالث في بيان أنه يمتنع كون ذات الله حاصلة في حيز معين على سبيل الوجوب : أنه لو حصل في حيز معين مع أنه يمتنع عليه أن ينتقل من ذلك الحيز إلى حيز آخر ، لزم أن يقال : إنه كالزمن المقعد ، العاجز عن الانتقال والحركة والجسم الحي الذي يكون موصوفا بهذه الصفة يكون في غاية النقص والعجز ، وتعالى الله عنه علوا كبيرا .
The third aspect in explaining that it is impossible for the essence of God to occur in a specific place necessarily: that if it occurred in a specific place with the impossibility of moving from that place to another, it would necessarily be said that it is like a crippled old man, incapable of motion and movement, and a living body described with this attribute is in the utmost deficiency and incapacity, and God is exalted above that by a great exaltation.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof that Allah cannot be necessarily in a specific place. The argument is straightforward: if Allah were necessarily confined to one locus and could not move to another, then He would resemble a paralyzed or disabled person who cannot change position. Such a description implies deficiency and incapacity, which cannot apply to Allah. Therefore, the claim that Allah is necessarily in a specific place is false. The author uses an analogy ('crippled old man') to highlight the absurdity of attributing such a state to the Perfect Being.

Key Terms
الحيز (al-hayyiz)
الانتقال (al-intiqal)
العجز (al-'ajz)
الزمن المقعد (al-zaman al-muq'ad)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that necessary localization does not imply inability to move; perhaps one could be fixed but still have power to move elsewhere.
Correction: The argument assumes necessary localization means being fixed in one place with the impossibility of moving. If movement were possible, the localization would not be necessary. Thus the analogy correctly identifies the implication.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Fourth Proof: Undermining the Argument for Contingency
The fourth proof that necessary localization would undermine the proof of the world's contingency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the fourth proof demonstrates that accepting necessary localization for God would undermine the standard proof of the world's contingency.

Core Idea
Necessary localization would allow eternal bodies, breaking the contingency argument.

This passage presents the fourth and perhaps most incisive proof against the idea that God could be necessarily located in a specific direction. The author shows that if such necessary localization were possible for God, then by extension, some bodies could also be necessarily located and thus eternal. This would completely dismantle the famous proof of the contingency of bodies (the argument for the world's creation). Let's see how this logical consequence unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the conditional structure starting with 'if it were permissible...'
2
Identify the core logical move
Notice that the author argues: if necessary localization is allowed for anything, then it could also be claimed for some bodies. This is the key step.
3
Understand the consequence
If some bodies are necessarily located, they cannot move, and thus the proof of contingency (which relies on movement/change) cannot be applied to them. The opponent loses certainty that all bodies are contingent.
4
Reflect on the rhetorical question
The passage ends with a rhetorical challenge: 'why is it not permissible for many bodies to exist outside the world necessarily?' This shows the absurdity of the opponent's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الرابع في بيان فساد هذا القسم : إنه لو جاز في شيء مختص بجهة معينة. أن يقال : إن اختصاصه بتلك الجهة واجب ، جاز أيضا ادعاء أن بعض الأجسام حصل في حيز معين، على سبيل الوجوب ، بحيث يمتنع خروجه عنه . وعلى هذا التقدير فلا يتمشى دليل حدوث الأجسام في كل الأجسام . لأنه يقال : لم لا يجوز وجود أجسام كثيرة مختصة بأحياز خارج العالم ، بحيث يمتنع عليها الانتقال ، وحينئذ لا يجري دليلكم على حدوث الأجسام في كلها ؟ وقائل هذا القول لا يمكنه القطع بحدوث كل الأجسام .
The fourth aspect in explaining the corruption of this division: that if it were permissible regarding something specific to a particular direction to say that its specification to that direction is necessary, then it would also be permissible to claim that some bodies occur in a specific place necessarily, such that their exit from it is impossible. And on this assumption, the proof of the contingency of bodies would not apply to all bodies. Because it would be said: why is it not permissible for many bodies to exist, specific to loci outside the world, such that movement from them is impossible? And then your proof of the contingency of bodies would not apply to all of them. And the proponent of this statement cannot be certain of the contingency of all bodies.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof against the claim that Allah is necessarily in a specific place. The author argues that if it were possible for something to be necessarily localized (i.e., its place is necessary), then one could also claim that some bodies (other than God) are necessarily in their places, unable to move. This would undermine the famous proof of the contingency of bodies (the kalam cosmological argument), which relies on the premise that all bodies are contingent and thus originated. If some bodies could be necessarily placed, then the proof cannot be applied universally, and one cannot be certain that all bodies are contingent. Therefore, accepting necessary localization for God opens the door to eternal bodies, which is absurd from a creationist perspective.

Key Terms
الجهة (al-jiha)
دليل حدوث الأجسام (dalil huduth al-ajsam)
الوجوب (al-wujub)
الامتناع (al-imtina')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Necessary localization could only apply to God, not to bodies.
Correction: The author shows that if it is possible for God, then by logical symmetry it is possible for bodies, which would then be eternal and uncreated.

Checkpoint
What does the fourth proof argue would happen if necessary localization were allowed?
A) It would prove that God is in a place.
B) It would allow the existence of eternal bodies outside the world.
C) It would strengthen the proof of contingency.
D) It would make all bodies necessarily located.

Key Takeaway
The fourth proof exposes that accepting necessary localization for Allah would logically allow eternal bodies, thus refuting the contingency argument for creation.

Fifth Proof: Dependency on Place Implies Contingency
The fifth proof that necessary localization would make Allah dependent on another being.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that necessary localization would entail God's dependence on another existent, leading to contingency, which is impossible for the Necessary Being.

Core Idea
Necessary localization makes God dependent on another, implying contingency.

This fifth proof addresses the assumption that God must be in a specific place. The author argues that such necessary localization would require that place to be essentially distinct from all others, making it an existing entity. Consequently, God's existence would rely on that entity, a clear sign of contingency that is incompatible with the divine nature. Let's unpack this logical chain step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Pay attention to the conditional structure: 'if it were necessary... then...'. This is a deductive argument that moves from a hypothesis to an impossibility.
Notice how the author uses logical reasoning without relying on scripture.
2
Identify the key logical steps
Break down the argument: (1) If God must be in one specific place, that place is essentially different from others; (2) Difference in essence implies existence; (3) Therefore, God's existence depends on that place; (4) Dependence on another is a property of contingent beings; (5) Contingency is impossible for God.
Each step builds on the previous one.
3
Understand the conclusion
The argument shows that necessary localization leads to a contradiction: the Necessary Being would become contingent. This refutes the idea that God is confined to a particular location.
The conclusion is that necessary localization is impossible.
4
Reflect on the implication for divine transcendence
Consider why this proof is important for Islamic theology: it reinforces God's independence (al-ghani) and transcendence above physical constraints.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الخامس في بيان فساد هذا القسم : هو أنه لو كان واجب الحصول في حيز معين ، وكان ممتنع الحصول في سائر الأحياز، فحينئذ يكون ذلك الحيز مخالفا بالماهية لسائر الأحياز، إذ لو كان مساويا لسائرها ، لوجب تساويها في جميع اللوازم والآثار ، ولو كانت الأحياز مختلفة بالماهية والحقيقة ، لكانت أمورا موجودة . فإذا قلنا : إن الباري تعالى يجب حصوله في الحيز المعين ، فحينئذ بلزم افتقاره في وجوده وتحققه إلى وجود غيره ، ولو كان الأمر كذلك ، لكان ممكنا لذاته ، وذلك محال .
The fifth aspect in explaining the corruption of this division: that if it were necessary for [Him] to occur in a specific place, and impossible for [Him] to occur in all other places, then that place would be different in essence from other places. For if it were equal to them, then they would be equal in all necessary consequences and effects. And if the places were different in essence and reality, they would be existing things. So if we say: the Creator the Exalted must occur in that specific place, then it would follow that He depends in His existence and reality on the existence of another. And if that were the case, He would be contingent by essence, and that is impossible.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof against necessary localization. The author argues that if God must be in a specific place and cannot be elsewhere, then that place must be essentially different from all other places. If it were not different, then all places would be equal in their properties, and the necessity of being in one would apply to all. But if it is different, then the place is an existing thing with its own essence. Consequently, God's existence would depend on that place, meaning He requires something else to exist. This is a sign of contingency (imkan), which is impossible for the Necessary Being. Thus, necessary localization is refuted.

Key Terms
الماهية (al-mahiyya)
اللوازم (al-lawazim)
الآثار (al-athar)
الافتقار (al-iftiqar)
الممكن (al-mumkin)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The place is not an existent thing; it is just a location without reality.
Correction: The author argues that if the place is essentially distinct from others, it must be an existing entity. A location that has a unique essence cannot be a mere void; it is a real thing. Thus, God's dependence on it would be on another existent, which entails contingency.

Checkpoint
Why does the fifth proof conclude that necessary localization makes God contingent?
A) Because the place is eternal and God depends on it.
B) Because the place is different in essence, so God's existence relies on that existent place.
C) Because God cannot move, so He is weak.
D) Because the argument assumes places are infinite.

Key Takeaway
Necessary localization would make God dependent on a distinct place, implying contingency—impossible for the Necessary Being.

Commit to one specific reminder this week to turn to Him in sincerity.

Contingent Localization and Its Impossibility
The author begins to refute contingent localization with the first proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why contingent localization of Allah is impossible, as it implies motion and rest and thus dependence.

Core Idea
Contingent localization leads to dependence, impossible for Allah.

The author now turns to the second division of the claim about Allah's location: that He is in a specific place contingently. This might seem less problematic than necessary localization, but it still leads to unacceptable consequences. The passage presents the first proof, focusing on the implications of motion and rest.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author introduces the second division and immediately states it is impossible.
The passage is cut off; focus on the logical structure given.
2
Identify the claim and the refutation
The claim is that Allah occurs in a specific place contingently. The author says this is impossible for several aspects, then begins the first aspect.
This is a classic refutation format: claim → impossibility → proof.
3
Analyze the first proof
The proof states that if contingent localization were true, then motion and rest would be valid for Allah. This would mean His essence is not free from them, implying dependence (iftiqar).
Think why motion and rest are problematic: they are accidents that require a subject, and the subject's relationship to them is contingent, implying need.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Even though the text cuts off, the intended conclusion is clear: dependence contradicts Allah's necessity. Therefore contingent localization is impossible.

Source Text

As for the second division, which is that it is said: He occurred in the specific place contingently, we say: this is impossible for several aspects. The first: since motion and rest are valid for Him, then His essence is not free of them, so His essence is dependent - it is impossible...

This would imply that His essence is not free from these accidents, meaning He is dependent (muftaqir) on something else to determine whether He moves or rests. The incomplete sentence 'His essence is dependent – it is impossible' hints that such dependence is incompatible with divine necessity. The text ends here, but the overall argument is that contingent localization also entails deficiency.

Fourth Proof: Reductio Against Necessary Location
Al-Razi gives the fourth proof against God's necessary spatial location via reductio.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi uses a reductio argument to show that God's necessary spatial location leads to an unacceptable consequence.

Core Idea
If God's location were necessary, then some bodies could be necessarily located, undermining proofs of creation.

Al-Razi now presents a fourth argument against the view that God is necessarily in a specific direction. This argument is a reductio ad absurdum: it shows that accepting necessary location leads to a consequence that undermines a key proof for the world's temporal origination. The argument forces the opponent to choose between giving up the claim or accepting a larger problem.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the logical flow starting with 'If it were permissible...' and the conclusion that the proof of temporal origination would not apply to all bodies.
This is a reductio argument, so follow the 'if... then...' chain.
2
Identify the reductio structure
Al-Razi assumes the opponent's position (necessary location) and derives a consequence that the opponent cannot accept. Identify what the consequence is and why it is problematic.
The consequence is that the proof of temporal origination would not be universal.
3
Understand the significance
Reflect on why this argument is effective. It forces the opponent to either deny necessary location or give up certainty on the temporal origination of all bodies. Which is more fundamental?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الرابع في بيان فساد هذا القسم : إنه لو جاز في شيء مختص بجهة معينة. أن يقال : إن اختصاصه بتلك الجهة واجب ، جاز أيضا ادعاء أن بعض الأجسام حصل في حيز معين، على سبيل الوجوب ، بحيث يمتنع خروجه عنه . وعلى هذا التقدير فلا يتمشى دليل حدوث الأجسام في كل الأجسام . لأنه يقال : لم لا يجوز وجود أجسام كثيرة مختصة بأحياز خارج العالم ، بحيث يمتنع عليها الانتقال ، وحينئذ لا يجري دليلكم على حدوث الأجسام في كلها ؟ وقائل هذا القول لا يمكنه القطع بحدوث كل الأجسام .
The fourth aspect in explaining the corruption of this division: If it were permissible for something specific to a particular direction to be said: its specification to that direction is necessary, then it would also be permissible to claim that some bodies occupy a specific location necessarily, such that it is impossible for them to leave it. On this assumption, the proof of the temporal origination of bodies would not apply to all bodies. Because it could be said: Why is it not permissible that there exist many bodies specific to locations outside the world, such that transition from them is impossible, and then your proof of the temporal origination of bodies would not apply to all of them? And the proponent of this statement cannot be certain of the temporal origination of all bodies.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage gives the fourth proof against the claim that God is necessarily in a specific direction. The argument proceeds by reductio ad absurdum: if it were permissible to say that something is necessarily in a specific direction, then it would also be permissible to claim that certain bodies are necessarily in specific locations outside the world. If that were the case, then the standard proof of the temporal origination of bodies (which assumes all bodies are contingent and thus originated) would not apply to all bodies, because some bodies could be necessary in their location. But the proponent of God's necessary location cannot be certain that all bodies are originated, thus the proof fails unless we reject the claim. This shows that the assumption leads to an undesirable consequence.

Key Terms
جهة
حيز
وجوب
حدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The fourth proof directly proves that God has no direction at all.
Correction: The proof is a reductio against the claim that God's location is necessary, not against the mere possibility of direction. It shows that if necessary location were true, it leads to an absurd outcome.

Checkpoint
What does the fourth proof argue would follow if God's being in a direction were necessary?
A) That bodies can also be necessarily located, undermining the proof of their origination.
B) That God would be in two directions.
C) That the world would be eternal.
D) That God would be composite.

Key Takeaway
The fourth proof shows that claiming necessary location for God leads to a breakdown of a universal proof of creation, thus the claim must be false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The reductio forces you to follow an idea to its end. Is there a belief you have about God that you have never fully examined because you sense it might lead to a contradiction? Will you trace it to its conclusion today?

Al-Razi's Fifth Proof: The Impossibility of Necessary Location
Al-Razi gives the fifth proof and concludes that necessary spatial location is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's fifth proof that God cannot be necessarily bound to a specific location, and why this argument reinforces divine transcendence.

Core Idea
If God were bound to a location, He would depend on it — but the Necessary Being depends on nothing.

Al-Razi continues his critique of the claim that God necessarily occupies a spatial location. He presents a fifth argument that exposes the logical flaw in such a view. By examining what it would mean for a location to be necessary for God, he shows it leads to dependence and thus undermines God's necessity. Let's follow his reasoning closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the flow of the argument.
The Arabic uses concise logical language.
2
Identify the conditional premise
Notice that the proof begins with the assumption that God necessarily obtains in a specific location.
The proof is structured as a conditional argument.
3
Understand the deduction about location
The proof argues that if the location is necessary for God, it must differ in essence from other locations, and thus be an existent thing.
This step is crucial: differing essences imply reality.
4
Grasp the entailment of dependence
If the location is an existent thing necessary for God's existence, then God depends on it, which contradicts His necessity.
Dependence implies contingency.
5
See the conclusion
The proof concludes that it is impossible for God to be necessarily in any specific location. This conclusion is established by all five proofs together.
This conclusion is a key tenet of divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الخامس في بيان فساد هذا القسم : هو أنه لو كان واجب الحصول في حيز معين ، وكان ممتنع الحصول في سائر الأحياز، فحينئذ يكون ذلك الحيز مخالفا بالماهية لسائر الأحياز، إذ لو كان مساويا لسائرها ، لوجب تساويها في جميع اللوازم والآثار ، ولو كانت الأحياز مختلفة بالماهية والحقيقة ، لكانت أمورا موجودة . فإذا قلنا : إن الباري تعالى يجب حصوله في الحيز المعين ، فحينئذ بلزم افتقاره في وجوده وتحققه إلى وجود غيره ، ولو كان الأمر كذلك ، لكان ممكنا لذاته ، وذلك محال فيثبت بهذه الوجوه الخمسة : أنه يمتنع أن يقال : إنه حصل في حيز معين على سبيل الوجوب
The fifth aspect in explaining the corruption of this division: If He were necessarily obtaining in a specific location and impossible to obtain in other locations, then that location would be different in essence from other locations, because if it were equal to others, they would necessarily be equal in all concomitants and effects. And if the locations are different in essence and reality, then they would be existent things. So if we say that God the Exalted necessarily obtains in that specific location, then it would entail His need in His existence and realization for the existence of something else. And if that were the case, He would be possible in essence, and that is impossible. Thus it is established by these five proofs that it is impossible to say that He is obtained in a specific location necessarily.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage delivers the fifth proof and its conclusion. The proof argues that if God were necessarily in a specific location, that location would differ in essence from other locations. If locations are different in essence, they are existent things. Then God's existence would depend on that location, making Him dependent and thus possible in essence. Since God is necessary, this is impossible. The conclusion sums up the first five proofs: it is impossible that God is in a specific location necessarily.

Key Terms
ماهية
لوازم
افتقار
إمكان
حيز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God is necessarily bound to a specific location such as the Throne.
Correction: This proof shows that if God were bound, He would depend on that location, which contradicts His necessity. Therefore, He transcends all spatial constraints.

Checkpoint
What is the key conclusion of the fifth proof?
A) That if God were necessarily in a location, that location would differ from others and thus God would depend on it.
B) That God is everywhere.
C) That locations are not real.
D) That God is moving.

Key Takeaway
God cannot be necessarily bound to any location, as that would make Him dependent; He is transcendent and free from spatial constraints.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

You may have grown up imagining God as being 'above' or in a certain direction. This passage declares that God cannot be spatially bound at all. How does that challenge your worship—do you ever mentally confine God to a place? What concrete step will you take to purify your conception of His transcendence?

Refuting God's Contingent Location
Al-Razi gives two arguments against God's contingent location.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Razi argues that it is impossible for God to be in a location contingently, and how his two arguments expose the logical contradictions in that claim.

Core Idea
If God's location is contingent, then God would be needy and originated—impossible for the Necessary Being.

Al-Razi now addresses the second possibility: that God might be in a specific location not by necessity but by contingency. This might seem more plausible than the first, but al-Razi shows it leads to even clearer absurdities. His two arguments cut to the heart of why any kind of location for God is rationally impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how al-Razi presents two distinct arguments, each leading to a contradiction.
The first argument uses motion/rest, the second uses the need for a specifier.
2
Understand the first argument
Focus on the first argument: if motion and rest are possible for God, then His essence is not specific to either, yet it cannot be free from them. This implies need and thus possibility, contradicting His necessity.
Al-Razi uses the principle that whatever depends on something else is possible.
3
Understand the second argument
The second argument: if God's location is contingent, a specifier is needed. That specifier's action makes the location originated. Since God cannot be free from that location, He would be originated—impossible.
This argument uses the kalām cosmological principle that whatever is not free from originated things is itself originated.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Notice how al-Razi concludes: both possibilities (necessary location and contingent location) are false, so God being in any location is impossible. This is a strong rational proof for divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني وهو أن يقال : إنه حصل في الحيز المعين على سبيل الجواز : فنقول : هذا محال لوجوه : الأول : إنه لما صح عليه الحركة والسكون ، فحينئذ لا تكون ذاته مخصوصة، مقتضية لواحد منهما مع يمتنع خلو ذاته عنهما ، فذاته مفتقرة إليهما ، وكل واحد منهما مفتقر إلى سبب منفصل ، والموقوف على الموقوف على الشيء ، موقوف على ذلك الشيء فيلزم افتقار ذات الله تعالى إلى شيء غيره ، وكل ما كان كذلك فهو ممكن لذاته فالواجب لذاته ممكن لذاته وذلك محال . الثاني : إنه إذا كان حصوله في الحيز المعين من الجائزات ، امتنع أن يحصل في حيز من الأحياز إلا بتخصيص مخصص ، ويجعل جاعل ، وكل ما حصل بفعل فاعل مختار ، فهو محدث. فيلزم أن يكون حصوله في الحيز المعين محدثا . وإذا امتنع خلو ذاته عن الحصول في الحيز المعين ، وثبت أن الحصول في الحيز المعين محدث ، لزم أن يقال : إن ذاته لا تخلو عن المحدث ، وما لا يخلو عن المحدث فهو محدث ، فيلزم أن تكون ذاته محدثة ، وهو محال . فيثبت بما ذكرنا : أنه تعالى لو حصل في حيز ، فالحصول فيه إما مع الوجوب أو مع الجواز. وثبت فساد كل واحد من هذين القسمين ، فوجب القطع بامتناع حصوله في الحيز والجهة
As for the second division, which is that it is said: He obtains in the specific location contingently, we say: This is impossible for reasons: First: Because motion and rest are possible for Him, so then His essence is not specific, requiring one of them while it is impossible for His essence to be free of them, so His essence is needy of them, and each of them is needy of a separate cause, and that which depends on that which depends on something depends on that something, so it necessitates the need of God's essence for something else. And everything that is like that is possible in essence, so the Necessary in essence would be possible in essence, and that is impossible. Second: If His obtaining in the specific location is among the contingencies, it is impossible for Him to obtain in any location except by specification from a specifier and a maker, and everything that occurs by the action of a free agent is originated. So it follows that His obtaining in the specific location is originated. And if it is impossible for His essence to be free from obtaining in that specific location, and it is established that His obtaining in that specific location is originated, then it must be said that His essence is not free from what is originated, and whatever is not free from what is originated is itself originated, so it follows that His essence is originated, and that is impossible. Thus it is established by what we have mentioned: that if the Exalted obtains in a location, His obtaining therein is either necessarily or contingently. And the corruption of each of these two divisions has been established, so it is necessary to judge the impossibility of His obtaining in location and direction.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage addresses the second possibility: that God is in a specific location contingently. Al-Razi gives two arguments. The first: if God has potential for motion and rest, His essence must be something that can be characterized by them, but He cannot be free from them, so He is needy. That leads to possibility. The second: if His location is contingent, it requires a specifier. That specifier's action makes the location originated. Since God cannot be free from that originated location, He would be originated. Both conclusions are impossible, so contingent location is also ruled out.

Misconception: Some may think that God being in a location is a matter of choice (contingent) rather than necessity, and thus avoid the problems of necessary location.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that contingency leads to even worse consequences: it makes God originated and dependent on a specifier.

Checkpoint

A) God would be composite.
B) God would be possible in essence.
C) God would be spatial.
D) God would be unknowable.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's two arguments show that contingent location for God leads to the impossible conclusions that God would be possible (not necessary) or originated (not eternal).
