?
The argument concludes that God cannot be in a location at all. How does this truth affect the way I approach prayer and du'a? Do I envision God in a specific direction, or do I internalize that He is beyond all spatial constraints?

Fifth Proof: Spherical Earth Against Divine Direction
Al-Razi argues from spherical earth to divine directionlessness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the spherical shape of the earth demonstrates that God cannot be confined to any spatial direction.

Core Idea
If the earth is round, direction is relative—God cannot be relative.

Al-Razi presents a clever cosmological proof. By observing a lunar eclipse, we can infer the earth is spherical. If the earth is a sphere, then 'up' and 'down' depend on where you stand. If God were in a particular direction, He would be 'down' for some people, which is absurd. This passage uses empirical observation to defend God's transcendence beyond space.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the author's own argument flow before analyzing.
2
Identify the two-part argument
Notice the two main claims: (1) the earth is a sphere, and (2) therefore God cannot be in any direction. The first part is proven by the lunar eclipse example.
The second part uses the relativity of 'up' and 'down'.
3
Reflect on the theological implication
Ask yourself why this argument refutes any notion of God being physically above us or in a specific location. How does the spherical earth make direction meaningless for God?
This connects to divine transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة في بيان أنه يمتنع حصول ذات الله تعالى في شيء من الأحياز والجهات : هو أن الأرض كرة ، وإذا كان كذلك امتنع كونه تعالى حاصلا في الحيز والجهة. أما بيان الأول فقد قررناه بالدلائل الكثيرة ، إلا أنا نذكر ههنا وجها واحداً ، وهو أنه إذا حصل خسوف قمري ، فإذا سألنا سكان أقصى المشرق عن أوله قالوا : إنه حصل في أول الليل ، وإذا سألنا سكان أقصى المغرب ، قالوا: إنه حصل في آخر الليل، فعلمنا أن أول الليل في أقصى المشرق هو آخر الليل في أقصى المغرب ، وذلك يوجب كون الأرض كرة . وإنما قلنا : إن الأرض لما كانت كرة ، امتنع كون الله تعالى حاصلا في شيء من الأحياز : هو أن الأرض إذا كانت كرة فالجهة التي هي فوق، بالنسبة إلى سكان أهل المشرق : هي تحت بالنسبة إلى سكان أهل المغرب ، وعلى العكس ، فلو حصل الباري تعالى في شيء من هذه الجهات، لكان تعالى في جهة التحت بالنسبة إلى بعض الناس ، وعلى العكس . وذلك باطل باتفاق العقلاء . فيثبت : أنه يمتنع كونه تعالى حيزا ، حاصلا في الحيز والجهة .
The fifth proof in explaining that it is impossible for the essence of God the Exalted to obtain in any of the locations and directions: it is that the earth is a sphere, and if that is the case, then it is impossible for Him the Exalted to be obtaining in location and direction. As for the explanation of the first [claim], we have already established it with many proofs, but here we mention one aspect: when a lunar eclipse occurs, if we ask the inhabitants of the furthest east about its beginning, they say it occurred at the beginning of the night, and if we ask the inhabitants of the furthest west, they say it occurred at the end of the night. So we know that the beginning of the night in the furthest east is the end of the night in the furthest west, and that necessitates that the earth is a sphere. And we say: because the earth is a sphere, it is impossible for God the Exalted to be obtaining in any location: because if the earth is a sphere, then the direction that is above for the inhabitants of the east is below for the inhabitants of the west, and vice versa. So if the Creator the Exalted were to obtain in any of these directions, He would be in a downward direction for some people, and the opposite. And that is false by consensus of rational people. Thus it is established that it is impossible for Him to be a location, obtaining in location and direction.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents a proof based on the spherical shape of the earth. Al-Razi notes that during a lunar eclipse, the time difference between east and west shows the earth is spherical. If the earth is spherical, then 'up' and 'down' are relative to the observer. If God were in a specific direction, He would be 'down' for some people, which is absurd. Therefore, God cannot be in any direction.

Misconception: God exists in a specific physical direction, such as 'above' the earth.
Correction: The spherical earth argument shows that 'above' is relative. If God were in a direction, He would be 'down' for half the world, which is absurd. Therefore, God transcends all directions.

The Fifth Proof: Earth's Sphericity Prevents Divine Location
Al-Razi presents the fifth proof that God is not in a place, based on earth's sphericity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Razi uses the sphericity of the earth to prove that God cannot be located in any physical place or direction.

Core Idea
Relative directions prove God cannot be confined to any location.

Al-Razi presents a philosophical proof rooted in an observable phenomenon—the lunar eclipse. He first demonstrates that the earth is a sphere, then argues that if 'above' and 'below' are relative to the observer, God cannot be in any particular direction. This lesson unpacks the logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through.
Notice the two-part structure: first proving the earth is a sphere, then deriving the conclusion.
2
Understand the lunar eclipse argument
Focus on how Al-Razi uses the difference in observed eclipse times between east and west to infer the earth's spherical shape.
This is an empirical argument, which is unusual in kalam; it shows engagement with natural science.
3
Grasp the relativity of directions
From the sphericity, Al-Razi concludes that directions like 'above' and 'below' are relative. Consider: what is above for easterners is below for westerners.
If God were in a specific direction, He would be 'below' for some people, which is absurd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة في بيان أنه يمتنع حصول ذات الله تعالى في شيء من الأحياز والجهات : هو أن الأرض كرة ، وإذا كان كذلك امتنع كونه تعالى حاصلا في الحيز والجهة
أما بيان الأول فقد قررناه بالدلائل الكثيرة ، إلا أنا نذكر ههنا وجها واحداً ، وهو أنه إذا حصل خسوف قمري ، فإذا سألنا سكان أقصى المشرق عن أوله قالوا : إنه حصل في أول الليل ، وإذا سألنا سكان أقصى المغرب ، قالوا: إنه حصل في آخر الليل، فعلمنا أن أول الليل في أقصى المشرق هو آخر الليل في أقصى المغرب ، وذلك يوجب كون الأرض كرة . وإنما قلنا : إن الأرض لما كانت كرة ، امتنع كون الله تعالى حاصلا في شيء من الأحيـاز : هو أن الأرض إذا كانت كرة فالجهة التي هي فوق، بالنسبة إلى سكان أهل المشرق : هي تحت بالنسبة إلى سكان أهل المغرب ، وعلى العكس ، فلو حصل الباري تعالى في شيء من هذه الجهات، لكان تعالى في جهة التحت بالنسبة إلى بعض الناس ، وعلى العكس . وذلك باطل باتفاق العقلاء . فيثبت : أنه يمتنع كونه تعالى حيزا ، حاصلا في الحيز والجهة .
The fifth proof in demonstrating that it is impossible for the essence of God Most High to occur in any of the places and directions: [it is] that the earth is a sphere, and if it is so, then it is impossible for Him to be occurring in place and direction. As for the demonstration of the first [claim], we have established it with many proofs, except that we mention here one aspect: that when a lunar eclipse occurs, if we ask the inhabitants of the far east about its beginning, they say: it occurred at the beginning of the night, and if we ask the inhabitants of the far west, they say: it occurred at the end of the night. So we know that the beginning of the night in the far east is the end of the night in the far west, and that necessitates that the earth is a sphere. And we only say: since the earth is a sphere, it is impossible for God Most High to occur in any of the places, [and that is] because if the earth is a sphere, then the direction that is above relative to the inhabitants of the east is below relative to the inhabitants of the west, and conversely. So if the Creator occurred in any of these directions, then He would be in a downward direction relative to some people, and conversely. And that is false by consensus of the rational people. So it is established: that it is impossible for Him to be a place, occurring in place and direction.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a proof (al-hujjah al-khamisah) demonstrating that God cannot be located in any place or direction. The argument proceeds in two steps. First, the author establishes that the earth is a sphere, using the empirical observation of a lunar eclipse. He notes that observers at the far east and far west report different times for the same eclipse—the east sees it at the beginning of the night, the west at the end—which proves that the earth must be spherical. Second, from this sphericity, he argues that any given direction is relative: what is 'above' for easterners is 'below' for westerners. If God were located in any specific direction, He would be above some and below others, which is absurd by universal rational agreement. Therefore, God cannot be in a place or direction at all. The proof relies on observable phenomena and rational consensus, not scriptural citation, making it a philosophical demonstration.

جهة
كرة
فوق
تحت
خسوف قمري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'above' is an absolute direction, and God is literally above the heavens.
Correction: This proof shows that 'above' is relative to the observer's location on a spherical earth, so it cannot apply to a transcendent God.

Key Takeaway

The Sixth Proof: God Cannot Be in a Place
Al-Razi presents the sixth proof that God cannot be in a place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth proof that God cannot be in a place, and how the void's temporality prevents God from being inside or outside the world.

Core Idea
The void is temporal, so the eternal God cannot dwell in it.

In this proof, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi examines the two possibilities for God's location: inside the world or outside. He shows that both lead to absurdities, primarily because the void—the space outside the world—is itself created and cannot contain the eternal Creator. This lesson walks through the logical steps of this argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the overall structure
Notice the proof divides into two main parts: examining why God cannot be inside the world, then why He cannot be outside the world. The second part further splits into finite vs. infinite void.
The proof is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
2
Follow the argument for the finite void
Al-Razi argues that if the void is finite, it has a shape. Since the void is a simple nature, its shape must come from a free agent, making the void temporal. Hence, God—who is eternal—cannot be in it without change.
This is the core of the proof.
3
Consider the infinite void and the objection
The infinite void is impossible for two reasons. Then consider and refute the objection that God could be in all infinite places simultaneously.
The passage cuts off mid-sentence but the refutation is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة في إثبات هذا المطلوب : أن نقول : لو حصل الباري تعالى في الحيز ، لحصل إما في العالم، أو خارج العالم . والقسمان باطلان ، فالقول بحصول الله تعالى في الحيز والجهة محال . أما أنه يمتنع أن يحصل في العالم ، فبالاتفاق ، ولأنه يلزم أيضا أن يكون جزءا من أجزاء العالم ، ومخالطا له ، وذلك محال . وأما أنه يمتنع أن يحصل خارج العالم ، فلأن الخلاء إنا أن يكون متناهيا ، أو غير متناه . فإن كان متناهيا فكل متناه : شكل وشكله ليس من لوازم ذاته ، لأن الخلاء كما بينا طبيعة بسيطة فتكون طبيعة الجزء مساويا لطبيعة الكل ، فل كان المقتضى لذلك الشكل هو تلك الماهية ، أو شيء من لوازمها ، لزم أن يكون شكل الكل مساويا لشكل الجزء ، وذلك محال . فيثبت أن شكله يجب أن يكون حاصلا من الفاعل المختار فيكون محدثا ، والخلاء لا ينفك عن الشكل وما لا ينفك عن المحدث فهو محدث فالخلاء محدث ، والله تعالى قديم فوجب أن يقال : إنه في الأزل ما كان حاصلا في شيء من الأحياز والجهات فلو حصل في الأزل في شيء من الأحياز والجهات لزم وقوع التغير في تلك الذات من حيث إنها هي . وذلك محال . وأما القسم الثاني وهو أن الخلاء لا نهاية له : فهذا محال لوجهين : الأول : إن الدليل دل على امتناع وجود بعد لا نهاية له والثاني : إن الخلاء إذا كان متناه فلا يشير العقل إلى حيز معين ، إلا وفوقه حيز آخر ، فلو حصلت ذات الله تعالى في ذلك الحيز ، لكان قد حصل في التحت لا في الفوق ، وذلك محال . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، امتنع حصوله في حيز معين ، وظاهر أيضا أنه يمتنع حصوله في حيز مبهم ، وحينئذ يلزم القطع بامتناع حصوله في الحيز أصلاً فإن قالوا فلم لا يجوز أن يقال : إنه يحصل في جميع الأحياز التي لا نهاية لها ؟ فنقول : هذا أيضا محال ، لأنه إما أن يقال : إن الذات الواحدة حصلت في كل تلك الأحياز، أو يقال : إنه حصل في كل واحد من تلك الأحياز جزء من أجزاء تلك الذات. والأول محال لأنه
The sixth proof in proving this sought-after [conclusion]: that we say: if the Creator occurs in place, then He occurs either in the world or outside the world. Both divisions are false, so the statement that God occurs in place and direction is impossible. As for that it is impossible for Him to occur in the world, it is by agreement, and because it would also necessitate that He be a part of the parts of the world and intermingling with it, and that is impossible. And as for that it is impossible for Him to occur outside the world, it is because the void is either finite or infinite. If it is finite, then every finite [thing] has a shape, and its shape is not among the necessary concomitants of its essence, because the void, as we have shown, is a simple nature, so the nature of the part is equal to the nature of the whole. So if the determinant for that shape were that essence or something from its necessary concomitants, then it would necessitate that the shape of the whole be equal to the shape of the part, and that is impossible. So it is established that its shape must come from a free agent, so it is temporal, and the void is not free of shape, and whatever is not free of the temporal is temporal, so the void is temporal, and God Most High is eternal. So it is necessary to say: that in pre-eternity He was not occurring in any of the places and directions; so if He occurred in pre-eternity in any of the places and directions, it would necessitate the occurrence of change in that essence from the perspective that it is it. And that is impossible. And as for the second division, that the void is infinite: this is impossible for two reasons: first, the proof indicates the impossibility of the existence of an infinite dimension; second, the void, if it is finite, the intellect does not point to a specific place except that above it is another place. So if the essence of God Most High occurred in that place, then He would have occurred in the below, not in the above, and that is impossible. And if the matter is so, it is impossible for Him to occur in a specific place, and it is also apparent that it is impossible for Him to occur in an ambiguous place. And then it necessitates the certainty of the impossibility of His occurring in place at all. For if they say: why is it not permissible to say that He occurs in all infinite places? We say: this is also impossible, because it is either said that the one essence occurred in all those places, or it is said that He occurred in each one of those places as a part of the parts of that essence. The first is impossible because
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof (al-hujjah al-sadisah) that God cannot be in a place. It considers two possibilities: God being inside the world or outside. The first is rejected by consensus and because it would make God a part of the world and intermingle with it, which is impossible for the Creator. The second possibility requires examining the void (al-khala'). The void is either finite or infinite. If finite, it must have a shape, but since the void is a simple nature, its shape cannot be intrinsic; thus it must be given by a free agent, making it temporal (muhdath). Since the void is temporal and God is eternal, God cannot be in it—He would have been in it in pre-eternity only if it existed, but it didn't, and entering it later would entail change in His essence. If the void is infinite, that is impossible because an infinite dimension cannot exist, and because any specific place in a finite void would have something above it, so placing God there would put Him below, absurd. Thus, no specific or ambiguous place works. Finally, the objection that God could be in all infinite places is refuted: either a single essence would be in all places (impossible) or parts of His essence would be distributed (impossible). The proof is cut off here but the argument is clear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'outside the world' is a valid location for God.
Correction: This proof shows the void itself is temporal and cannot contain the eternal God.

Checkpoint
In the sixth proof, why is it impossible for God to be outside the world?
A) Because the void is infinite and cannot contain anything.
B) Because the void is temporal (created) and God is eternal, so He cannot be in it.
C) Because outside the world there is nothing, not even space.
D) Because the void has no shape to contain anything.

Key Takeaway
God cannot be in any place, because the void—the only possible location outside the world—is itself created and cannot contain the eternal Creator.

?

?

?

First Argument: God Is Not in Space Inside or Outside the World
Argument that God is not in space, using the impossibility of inside or outside the world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that God cannot be located in space, either inside the world or outside it, based on the nature of the void.

Core Idea
God cannot be in space because space is created, and He is eternal.

In this passage, the author presents the first of several arguments for God's transcendence beyond space and direction. He frames it as a dilemma: if God were in space, He would be either inside the world or outside it. Both options are impossible. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, especially the detailed proof that the void outside the world is created, so it cannot contain the eternal Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Notice how the author structures the argument as a dilemma.
The passage uses a conditional: 'if God were in space...'
2
Identify the two branches of the dilemma
The author splits the possibility into 'inside the world' and 'outside the world'. Understand that both are considered and then refuted.
3
Understand the refutation of 'inside the world'
The refutation is by consensus and by the logical consequence that God would be part of the world and mixed with it.
This is the simpler part.
4
Follow the detailed refutation of 'outside the world'
The author argues that the void outside is either finite or infinite. He examines the finite case, showing that the void's shape requires a creator, making it originated. Thus, the void is created, and God cannot be in it.
Pay attention to the logical steps: finite void has shape, shape is not essential, shape from free agent, void originated.
5
Understand the conclusion
Since the void is originated and God is eternal, God cannot be located in any space. Also, if He were in space in pre-eternity, that would imply change, impossible for God.
The final sentence ties back to God's immutability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعالى في الحيز ، لحصل إما في العالم، أو خارج العالم . والقسمان باطلان ، فالقول بحصول الله تعالى في الحيز والجهة محال . أما أنه يمتنع أن يحصل في العالم ، فبالاتفاق ، ولأنه يلزم أيضا أن يكون جزءا من أجزاء العالم ، ومخالطا له ، وذلك محال . وأما أنه يمتنع أن يحصل خارج العالم ، فلأن الخلاء إنا أن يكون متناهيا ، أو غير متناه . فإن كان متناهيا فكل متناه : شكل وشكله ليس من لوازم ذاته ، لأن الخلاء كما بينا طبيعة بسيطة فتكون طبيعة الجزء مساويا لطبيعة الكل ، فل كان المقتضى لذلك الشكل هو تلك الماهية ، أو شيء من لوازمها ، لزم أن يكون شكل الكل مساويا لشكل الجزء ، وذلك محال . فيثبت أن شكله يجب أن يكون حاصلا من الفاعل المختار فيكون محدثا ، والخلاء لا ينفك عن الشكل وما لا ينفك عن المحدث فهو محدث فالخلاء محدث ، والله تعالى قديم فوجب أن يقال : إنه في الأزل ما كان حاصلا في شيء من الأحياز والجهات [ فلو حصل في الأزل في شيء من الأحياز والجهات ] لزم وقوع التغير في تلك الذات من حيث إنها هي . وذلك محال .
He (God), exalted be He, is in space; thus He would occur either in the world or outside the world. Both divisions are false, so the statement that God, exalted be He, occurs in space and direction is impossible. As for His being impossible to occur in the world, it is by consensus, and because it would also necessitate that He be a part of the parts of the world and mixed with it, and that is impossible. As for His being impossible to occur outside the world, it is because the void is either finite or infinite. If it is finite, then everything finite has a shape, and its shape is not among the necessary concomitants of its essence, because the void, as we have shown, is a simple nature; thus the nature of the part equals the nature of the whole. If the requisite for that shape were that essence or something from its concomitants, it would necessitate that the shape of the whole equal the shape of the part, and that is impossible. Thus it is established that its shape must result from the free agent, so it is originated (muhdath). The void is not free of shape, and whatever is not free of the originated is originated, so the void is originated. God, exalted be He, is eternal (qadim), so it must be said: In pre-eternity (al-azal) He was not occurring in any of the spaces and directions. For if He occurred in pre-eternity in any of the spaces and directions, it would necessitate the occurrence of change in that essence inasmuch as it is itself, and that is impossible.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a proof refuting the claim that God is located in space (al-hayyiz) or direction (al-jiha). The author presents a dilemma: if God were in space, He would be either inside the world or outside the world. Both are invalid. Being inside the world is impossible by consensus and because it would make God a part of the world and mixed with it. Being outside the world is also impossible because the void (al-khala') outside is either finite or infinite. The author first examines the finite case: every finite thing has a shape, but that shape is not essential to the void's simple nature—otherwise the shape of the whole would equal the shape of the part. Thus the shape is caused by a free agent, making the void originated (muhdath). Whatever is inseparable from the originated is itself originated, so the void is originated. God is eternal (qadim), so He cannot be in an originated void; otherwise He would have changed. Therefore, God was not in any space or direction in pre-eternity, and being in one later would imply change, which is impossible.

القديم

Misconception: One might think that 'outside the world' is a neutral location that could accommodate God.
Correction: The author shows that the void itself is created (originated), so it cannot contain the eternal God.

Checkpoint
Why is it impossible for God to be outside the world according to the finite void argument?
A) Because the void has no shape
B) Because the void is originated and God is eternal
C) Because the void is part of the world
D) Because the void is infinite

Key Takeaway
God's eternal nature excludes the possibility of being located in any space or direction, because space itself is created.

In what areas of your life do you secretly wish He would change His rulings or attributes to suit your desires? How will you submit to His unchangeable perfection?

God Cannot Be in Infinite Void or All Spaces
Refutation of God being in infinite void and the objection that He could occupy all spaces.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that God exists in an infinite void or occupies all spaces is rationally impossible.

Core Idea
Space and direction are impossible for Allah, whether finite, infinite, or all-encompassing.

This passage tackles a sophisticated objection: if the void is infinite, could God be there? Or if not, could He occupy all spaces? The author systematically rules out each possibility, showing that any spatial relation to God leads to absurdities. This lesson traces the logical steps that affirm Allah's transcendence beyond physical location.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once through, then its literal translation. Notice the logical connectors that structure the argument.
2
Identify the main arguments
The passage contains three main refutations: (1) infinite void is impossible, (2) any specific space would put God in the lower, (3) occupying all spaces is also impossible. Locate each part.
Look for 'القسم الثاني', 'فإن قالوا', and the two possibilities.
3
Understand the 'all spaces' objection
The objection suggests God could occupy all infinite spaces. The author presents two possibilities: either the whole essence in each space or a part in each. Both are refuted.
This refutation uses the same 'lower/upper' reasoning as before.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The final sentence states that the claim leads to false divisions, so it is impossible. Consider how this strengthens tanzih (divine transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني وهو أن الخلاء لا نهاية له : فهذا محال لوجهين : الأول : إن الدليل دل على امتناع وجود بعد لا نهاية له والثاني : إن الخلاء إذا كان متناه فلا يشير العقل إلى حيز معين ، إلا وفوقه حيز آخر ، فلو حصلت ذات الله تعالى في ذلك الحيز ، لكان قد حصل في التحت لا في الفوق ، وذلك محال . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، امتنع حصوله في حيز معين ، وظاهر أيضا أنه يمتنع حصوله في حيز مبهم ، وحينئذ يلزم القطع بامتناع حصوله في الحيز أصلاً فإن قالوا فلم لا يجوز أن يقال : إنه يحصل في جميع الأحياز التي لا نهاية لها ؟ فنقول : هذا أيضا محال ، لأنه إما أن يقال : إن الذات الواحدة حصلت في كل تلك الأحياز، أو يقال : إنه حصل في كل واحد من تلك الأحياز جزء من أجزاء تلك الذات. والأول محال لأنه يقتضي حصول الذات الواحدة بتمامها في الأحياز الكثيرة دفعة واحدة ، وذلك محال . ولأنه لما حصل ذلك الواحد في كل تلك الأحياز ، وكل واحد منها تحت حيز آخر ، فحينئذ يلزم أن تكون تلك الذات حصلت في التحت لا في الفوق . وهو محال . والثاني أيضا محال ، لأنه يقتضي كون تلك الذات مركبة مؤلفة . وأيضا : فكل واحد من تلك الأجزاء لما حصل في واحد من تلك الأحياز ، وقد ثبت أن كل واحد من تلك الأحياز المعينة ، فإنه تحت حيز آخر ، فحينئذ يعود ما ذكرنا إلى أنه تعالى حاصل في التحت ، لا في الفوق، وذلك محال . فيثبت : أن القول بكونه تعالى حاصلا في الحيز والجهة يفضي إلى هذه الأقسام الباطلة ، فوجب أن يكون القول به محالا
As for the second division—that the void has no end: this is impossible for two reasons. The first: Evidence indicates the impossibility of the existence of an infinite dimension. The second: If the void is finite, then the intellect does not point to a specific space without there being another space above it. So if the essence of God, exalted be He, occurred in that space, then He would have occurred in the lower, not the upper, and that is impossible. If this is the case, His occurrence in a specific space is impossible, and it is also apparent that His occurrence in an ambiguous space is impossible. Therefore, it necessarily follows the definitive impossibility of His occurrence in space at all. If they say: 'Why is it not permissible to say that He occurs in all spaces that have no end?' We say: This is also impossible, because it must be said either that the single essence occurs in all those spaces, or that in each of those spaces occurs a part of the parts of that essence. The first is impossible because it requires the single essence in its entirety to occur in many spaces at once, and that is impossible. And because when that one occurs in each of those spaces, and each of them is under another space, then it necessarily follows that that essence occurs in the lower, not the upper, and that is impossible. The second is also impossible because it requires that essence to be composed and aggregate. Also, when each of those parts occurs in one of those spaces, and it is established that each of those specific spaces is under another space, then what we mentioned returns: that He, exalted be He, occurs in the lower, not the upper, and that is impossible. Thus it is established: The statement that He, exalted be He, occurs in space and direction leads to these false divisions, so the statement must be impossible.

The argument then moves to: even if we consider specific spaces, any space has another above it, so if God is in a specific space, He would be in the lower, not the upper, which is improper. Then the author considers an objection: why not say God occupies all infinite spaces? He refutes this by two possibilities: either the single essence is in all spaces at once (impossible) or a part of Him in each space (making Him composite). Both lead to absurdity. The conclusion: the claim that God is in space leads to these false divisions, so it is impossible.

Seventh Proof: God Cannot Be in Space
Seventh proof that God cannot be in space: dichotomy and refutation with objection and answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seventh proof that God cannot be in space, based on the dichotomy that space must be either existent or non-existent, both of which are impossible for the Necessary Existence.

Core Idea
If God needed space, He would depend on something else – impossible for the Self-Sufficient.

This lesson presents the seventh of the arguments for God's transcendence above space and direction. The argument proceeds by considering the very nature of space: if God were to occupy it, would that space be something that exists or something that does not? Both alternatives lead to an impossibility. The author then addresses a powerful objection: does this same logic force us to say bodies are not in space? The response clarifies why the contingency of bodies makes all the difference.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dichotomy
The argument begins by stating that if God were in space, that space must be either existent or non-existent. Recognise this as an exhaustive division (ḥaṣr).
2
See why existent space is impossible
If space is existent, then God would need that existent space. But the Necessary of Existence (wājib al-wujūd) cannot need anything outside itself. This would contradict His self-sufficiency.
3
See why non-existent space is impossible
If space is non-existent, it is a pure nothing. A nothing cannot serve as a container (ẓarf) for God, nor can God be contained (maẓrūf) in it. This is rationally absurd.
4
Grasp the objection and its answer
An objector claims the same reasoning would show bodies cannot be in space. The author answers that bodies are possible in themselves (mumkin al-wujūd), so their need for space is not absurd. Only the Necessary Being's dependence would be absurd.
This distinction is crucial: contingency allows dependence; necessity does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة : لو كان الله تعالى حاصلا في الحيز والجهة ، لكان المسمى بالحيز والجهة ، إما أن يكون موجودا أو معدوما ، والقسمان باطلان ، فبطل القول بوجوب كونه تعالى في الحيز. أما الحصر فظاهر، وإما إبطال كون الحيز موجودا . فالدليل عليه : أنه امتنع خلو ذات الله تعالى عن الحصول في الحيز ، ولو كان الحيز أمرا موجودا ، لزم احتياج ذات الله تعالى إلى غيره ، وواجب الوجود لذاته يمتنع كونه محتاجا إلى الغير. وأما إبطال كون الحيز معدوما فلان المعدوم نفي محض وعدم صرف ، فجعله ظرفا لذات الله تعالى ، وجعل ذات الله مظروفا فيه : محال . فإن قيل : فهذا بعينه وارد في الأجسام فيلزم نفي كونها حاصلة في الأحياز، وذلك قول باطل . فتقول : الجواب عنه من وجهين : الأول : إنا نقول : الحيز والجهة أمر موجود ، وهو البعد المجرد والفضاء المحض ، فإذا قلنا : إن الجسم يحتاج إليه لم يلزم منه محال ، لأن الجسم ممكن الوجود لذاته، والقول يكون الممكن لذاته محتاجا إلى الغير ليس قولا باطلا . أما القول بأن واحب الوجود لذاته يحتاج إلى الغير فهو قول باطل فظهر الفرق
The seventh proof: If God, exalted be He, occurred in space and direction, then that which is called space and direction would be either existent or non-existent. Both divisions are false, so the statement that He, exalted be He, is necessarily in space is invalid. As for the exclusive division, it is apparent. As for invalidating the space being existent: The proof for it is that it is impossible for the essence of God, exalted be He, to be free from occurrence in space. If space were an existent thing, it would necessitate that the essence of God, exalted be He, need another, and the Necessary of Existence in itself (wajib al-wujud li-dhatihi) is impossible to be in need of another. As for invalidating the space being non-existent: because the non-existent is pure negation and absolute non-existence, so making it a container (zarf) for the essence of God, exalted be He, and making the essence of God contained (mazruf) in it is impossible. If it is said: 'This very same argument applies to bodies, necessitating the negation of their occurrence in spaces, and that is an invalid statement.' We say: The answer to it is from two aspects: First: We say: Space and direction are an existent thing, namely abstract dimension and pure void. So if we say that the body needs it, no absurdity follows, because the body is possible of existence in itself (mumkin al-wujud li-dhatihi), and the statement that the possible in itself is in need of another is not an invalid statement. As for the statement that the Necessary of Existence in itself needs another, it is an invalid statement. Thus the difference becomes clear.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh proof against God being in space. The author uses a dichotomy: the space/direction in which God would be is either existent or non-existent. Both options are impossible. If space is existent, then God would need that existent, but the Necessary of Existence (wajib al-wujud) cannot depend on another. If space is non-existent, then a non-entity cannot serve as a container for God. An objection is raised: the same reasoning would imply that bodies are not in space, which is false. The author answers with two points. First, space/direction is an existent thing—abstract dimension and pure void. When we say a body needs space, that is acceptable because the body is possible in itself (mumkin al-wujud), and a contingent thing needing something else is not absurd. However, the Necessary of Existence needing something else is absurd. Thus the difference is clear: God's case is unique because of His necessary existence.

موجود
معدوم
واجب الوجود
ممكن الوجود
ظرف
مظروف
البعد المجرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The same argument proves that bodies cannot occupy space either.
Correction: The argument only applies to the Necessary of Existence. Bodies are contingent (mumkin al-wujud), so their need for space does not entail absurdity.

Checkpoint
What is the answer to the objection that the same argument would prove bodies are not in space?
A) Bodies do not need space
B) Space is non-existent for bodies
C) Bodies are possible in themselves, so needing space is not absurd
D) The argument only applies to God

Key Takeaway
God cannot be in space because space would either exist and thus make God dependent, or not exist and thus be an impossible container; bodies, being contingent, can depend on space without contradiction.

?
In what subtle ways do you confine God to certain places (like only the masjid) or times (like only Ramadan)? Commit to one concrete change in your mindset or practice that acknowledges He is not contained by space.

The Seventh Argument: Disjunctive Syllogism Against Divine Location
Al-Razi presents the seventh argument against divine location, with objection and response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logic of Al-Razi's seventh argument against spatial location for Allah, including the objection and its two-part answer.

Core Idea
If Allah is in space, space must be existent or non-existent; both lead to absurdity for the Necessary Being.

This lesson presents Al-Razi's seventh argument against the idea that Allah occupies space. He constructs a careful disjunctive syllogism: spatial extension must be either existent or non-existent, and each option leads to a conclusion incompatible with Allah's nature as the Necessary Being. The passage also anticipates an objection from analogy with bodies and provides two distinct answers, deepening the argument.

Guided Path
1
Follow the disjunctive syllogism
Identify the two possibilities: space exists or does not exist. See how each possibility is refuted for Allah.
The argument hinges on the impossibility of Allah needing anything or being contained in nothing.
2
Examine the objection
Notice the potential counterexample: bodies are in space, so the same reasoning would deny that. How does Al-Razi respond?
The objection tries to show the argument proves too much.
3
Compare the two answers
The first answer distinguishes necessity vs. contingency; the second defines 'place' differently. Understand the difference and why each works.
Both answers rely on the unique status of the Necessary Being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة : لو كان الله تعالى حاصلا في الحيز والجهة ، لكان المسمى بالحيز والجهة ، إما أن يكون موجودا أو معدوما ، والقسمان باطلان ، فبطل القول بوجوب كونه تعالى في الحيز. أما الحصر فظاهر، وإما إبطال كون الحيز موجودا . فالدليل عليه : أنه امتنع خلو ذات [ الله تعالى عن الحصول في الحيز ، ولو كان الحيز أمرا موجودا ، لزم احتياج ذات الله تعالى (١) ] إلى غيره ، وواجب الوجود لذاته يمتنع كونه محتاجا إلى الغير. وأما إبطال كون الخيز معدوما [ فلان المعدوم (۲) ] نفي محض وعدم صرف ، فجعله ظرفا لذات الله تعالى ، وجعل ذات الله مظروفا فيه : محال .
فإن قيل : فهذا بعينه وارد في الأجسام فيلزم نفي كونها حاصلة في الأحياز، وذلك قول باطل . فتقول : الجواب عنه من وجهين :
الأول : إنا نقول : الحيز والجهة أمر موجود ، وهو البعد المجرد والفضاء المحض ، فإذا قلنا : إن الجسم يحتاج إليه لم يلزم منه محال ، لأن الجسم ممكن الوجود لذاته، والقول يكون الممكن لذاته محتاجا إلى الغير ليس قولا باطلا .
أما القول بأن واحب الوجود لذاته يحتاج إلى الغير فهو قول باطل فظهر الفرق
•
الوجه الثاني في الجواب : أن نقول : المكان إما أن يكون مفسرا بالبعد الذي ينفذ فيه الجسم ، أو بالسطح المحيط . فإن كان الحق هو الأول فالجواب ما ذكرناه في الوجه الأول . وهو فرق صحيح ، وإن كان الحق هو الثاني ، قلنا : إن كل العالم ليس في حيز وجهة البتة ، بل هو ذات مركبة من الأجزاء والأبعاض، فإن حكمتم بكون الباري تعالى كذلك ، كان ذلك قولا بأنه جسم مؤلف من الأجزاء ، وقد سبق بيان أن ذلك قول باطل
The seventh proof: If God Most High were located in space and direction, then what is called space and direction would either be existent or non-existent, and both divisions are invalid, so the assertion that God Most High must be in space is invalid. As for the division into two, it is obvious. As for invalidating space being existent, the proof for it is that it is impossible for the essence of God Most High to be devoid of being in space, and if space were an existent thing, then the essence of God Most High would need something other than itself, and the Necessary of Existence in Itself cannot be in need of another. As for invalidating space being non-existent, because the non-existent is pure negation and sheer nothing, so making it a container for the essence of God Most High and making the essence of God Most High contained in it is impossible. If it is said: This same argument applies to bodies, necessitating the denial of their being located in spaces, and that is a false statement. So we say: The answer to it is from two aspects: The first: We say: Space and direction are an existent thing, which is abstract dimension and pure void. So if we say that the body needs it, no impossibility follows from that, because the body is contingent in essence, and the statement that the contingent in essence needs another is not false. As for the statement that the Necessary of Existence in Itself needs another, that is false, so the difference is clear. The second aspect of the answer: We say: Place is either interpreted as the dimension into which the body penetrates, or as the surrounding surface. If the truth is the first, then the answer is what we mentioned in the first aspect, and that is a valid distinction. If the truth is the second, then we say: The whole world is not in any space or direction at all; rather it is an essence composed of parts and members. If you judge that the Creator Most High is likewise, that would be a statement that He is a body composed of parts, and it has already been shown that that is a false statement.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh argument (al-hujjah al-sābi‘ah) against the view that Allah is spatially located. The argument proceeds as a disjunctive syllogism: if Allah were in a spatial extension (al-ḥayyiz) or direction (al-jihah), then that spatial extension or direction must be either existent or non-existent. Both possibilities are shown to be impossible. If the spatial extension is existent, then Allah would be in need of it, which is impossible for the Necessary Being (wājib al-wujūd). If it is non-existent, then making a pure nothing a container for Allah is absurd. Thus the claim is invalid. The passage then addresses an objection: the same reasoning would apply to bodies, leading to denial of their location. The response has two aspects. First, spatial extension as abstract dimension or pure void is existent, and bodies as contingent can depend on it without contradiction. In contrast, the Necessary Being cannot depend on anything. Second, if 'place' is defined as the surrounding surface, then the entire world is not in a place; it is a composite of parts. If one likens Allah to that, it would imply Allah is composite, which is already refuted. The structure is: proof, objection, two-part answer.

Key Terms
حيز (ḥayyiz)
جهة (jihah)
موجود (mawjūd)
معدوم (ma‘dūm)
واجب الوجود (wājib al-wujūd)
مكان (makān)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The same argument would prove bodies are not in space.
Correction: Bodies are contingent and can depend on space, unlike the Necessary Being.

Checkpoint
According to the seventh argument, why is it impossible for spatial extension to be non-existent?
A) Because non-existence is a pure negation, making it impossible to serve as a container for Allah.
B) Because non-existence cannot be a container for anything.
C) Because the necessary being must be in something existent.
D) Because the objection shows it is possible for bodies.

Key Takeaway
The seventh argument shows that spatial location for Allah leads to impossibility whether space is existent or non-existent, and the objection from bodies is resolved by the contingency of bodies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah is beyond space and time, what does that mean for how you approach Him in your daily life? Are you tempted to confine Him to a particular place (like a mosque or a prayer mat)? How can you remind yourself that He is transcendent?
?
The argument shows that Allah cannot be contained by anything. In your heart, have you ever tried to contain Allah in your own understanding or assumptions? What would it mean to let go of that and worship a God who is beyond all categories?
?
If bodies are contingent and depend on space, but Allah is necessary and independent, does your reliance on created things reflect a lack of trust in Allah's self-sufficiency? How can you align your dependency solely on Him?

The Eighth Argument: Sensory Pointing and Divine Transcendence
Al-Razi proves that anything sensorily pointed to is either a body or an accident, and Allah is neither.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Razi uses the division of sensory pointing into body and accident to establish that Allah is not spatially located.

Core Idea
Anything pointed to as 'here' is either a body or an accident; Allah is neither, so He is beyond space.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents his eighth argument for Allah's transcendence. He begins by classifying anything that can be sensorily pointed to as 'here' or 'there' into two categories: if the pointing is primary and independent, it is a body; if secondary (inhering in another), it is an accident. Since it has already been established that Allah is neither a body nor an accident, the conclusion follows that He cannot occupy space or direction. This concise logical division is a powerful tool in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: a conditional premise followed by a division and then a conclusion.
The passage begins with 'الحجة الثامنة'.
2
Identify the two categories
Look for the words 'الأول' and 'الثاني'. The passage divides sensory pointing into primary (independent) and secondary (dependent). Associate each with 'body' and 'accident'.
3
Trace the logical chain
Follow the argument: from the division, apply the previously proven rejection of Allah being a body, and then note that He cannot be an accident either, leading to the final conclusion.
Pay attention to 'ولما دللنا في الفصل المتقدم'.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this argument matters for 'tanzih' (transcendence). How does it prevent corporealist conceptions of God?
This connects to the broader theme of Allah's incomparability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثامنة : إن كل ما صحت الإشارة الحسية إليـه بـأنـه ههنا أو هناك ، فإما أن يكون موصوفا بهذه الصفة على سبيل الأصالة والاستقلال ، أو على سبيل التبعية ، فإن كان الأول فهو الجسم ، وإن كان الثاني فهو العرض ، ولما دللنا في الفصل المتقدم على أنه يمتنع كونه جسما . وظاهر أنه أيضا ليس بعرض ، وإلا لكان محتاجا إلى المحل ، فحينئذ يلزم منه امتناع كونه حاصلا في الحيز والجهة . وهو المطلوب
The eighth proof: Everything to which sensory pointing is valid as 'here' or 'there' is either described with this attribute in a primary and independent manner, or in a secondary manner. If the first, it is the body (al-jism); if the second, it is the accident (al-‘araḍ). Since we have demonstrated in the preceding chapter that it is impossible for Him to be a body, and it is evident that He is also not an accident, otherwise He would need a substratum (al-maḥall). Therefore, it follows that it is impossible for Him to be located in space and direction. And that is what was sought.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage presents the eighth argument (al-ḥujjah al-thāminah). It classifies any entity subject to sensory pointing (ishāra ḥissiyya) as either a body (jism) if the pointing is primary and independent, or an accident (‘araḍ) if secondary (i.e., inhering in a body). Al-Razi asserts that it has already been proven that Allah cannot be a body, and obviously He is not an accident because accidents need a substratum. Therefore, Allah cannot be spatially located. The argument is a concise division leading to the desired conclusion (al-maṭlūb).

Key Terms
إشارة حسية
جسم
عرض
محل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might claim that sensory pointing does not necessarily imply corporeality; it could be a property of non-corporeal entities.
Correction: Al-Razi assumes, based on earlier definitions, that 'primary sensory pointing' is the defining feature of a body. For kalam, anything independently pointed to in space is a body by definition. The argument rests on that established classification.

Checkpoint
According to the eighth argument, if something can be pointed to sensorily in a primary and independent manner, what is it?
A) It is a body.
B) It is an accident.
C) It is a substratum.
D) It is a spiritual substance.

Key Takeaway
Sensory pointing implies either corporeality (body) or inherence (accident); since Allah is neither, He transcends spatial location.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you raise your hands in du'a, do you imagine Allah is in a particular direction? How does this argument challenge the orientation of your heart in worship?
?
Have you ever felt spiritually distant from Allah as if He were far away in space? How does knowing that He is not located in any direction reshape your understanding of His nearness?
?
This argument proves Allah is not in space. Yet, when you think of His throne (al-ʿarsh), do you still imagine a physical location? What must you purge from your concept of Allah to truly affirm His transcendence?

Spatial Extension Necessitates Parts
Al-Razi argues extended objects must have parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's argument that any spatially located, extended object must have parts because different parts face different directions.

Core Idea
Spatial extension forces parts.

Al-Razi presents his ninth argument against the possibility of Allah being spatially located. He begins by considering any object that can be pointed to and is large. Such an object inevitably has parts, because if it faced all directions identically, contradictions would arise.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the flow: premise, observation, conclusion.
Pay attention to the terms 'يمين العرش' and 'يسار العرش'.
2
Identify the key premise
The argument starts with 'everything pointed to by sensory perception and great'. Understand what 'مشار إليه' means in this context.
3
Follow the directional reasoning
The argument uses the example of facing the right and left of the Throne. See how this forces two distinct sides.
If both sides were identical, contradictions would occur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة : إن كل ما كان مشارا إليه بحب الحس ، وكان شيئا عظيما ، فإنه لا بد وأن نفرض فيه الأجزاء والأعضاء ، لأن الشيء الذي منه يحاذي يمين العرش ، غير الشيء الذي منه يحاذي يسار العرش ، وكيف لا نقول ذلك ونقول : بأن هذا الجانب يحاذي يمين العرش لا يساره ، والجانب الآخر منه يحاذي يسار العرش لا يمينه ؟ فلو كان الجانبان شيئا واحدا ، لزم اجتماع النفي والإثبات ، وأنه محال
وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : كل واحد من النصفين يماس النصف الآخر بأحد وجهيه دون الثاني . والوجهان متساويان في تمام الماهية ، والمتساويان في تمام الماهية ، يجب أن يصح على كل واحد منها ما يصح على الآخر ، وكما صح على أحد النصفين أن يماس النصف الآخر بأحد وجهيه دون الثاني ، وجب أن يصح عليه أن يماسه بالوجه الثاني دون الأول . ومتى صح ذلك ، لزم صحة التفرق والتمزق عليه ، فيثبت : أن كل ما حصل في الجهة والحيز ، وكان عظيم الذات ، فإنه يكون جسما مؤلفا من الأجزاء ، أو يكون التفرق والتمزق عليه
The ninth proof: Everything that is pointed to by sensory perception and is something great (magnitude), inevitably we must assume in it parts and limbs, because that from which it faces the right side of the Throne is other than that from which it faces the left side of the Throne. How could we not say that, and we say that this side faces the right of the Throne, not its left, and the other side faces the left of the Throne, not its right? So if the two sides were one thing, the conjunction of negation and affirmation would be necessary, and that is impossible. And when this is established, we say: Each of the two halves touches the other half with one of its two faces and not the other. And the two faces are equal in complete essence, and things equal in complete essence must have the same possibility as the other. Just as it is valid for one of the two halves to touch the other half with one of its two faces and not the other, so it must be valid for it to touch it with the second face and not the first. And whenever that is valid, the possibility of separation and fragmentation is necessary for it. Thus is established: Everything that occurs in direction and space and is great in essence must be a body composed of parts, or else separation and fragmentation are possible for it.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage presents the ninth argument (al-ḥujjah al-tāsi‘ah). It starts by considering a large object pointed to by sensory perception. Such an object must have parts because different parts face different directions—e.g., one side faces the right of the Throne, another the left. If both sides were identical, then contradictory attributions (facing right and not facing right) would apply, which is impossible. Then the argument considers two halves of such an object. Each half touches the other with one face but not the other. Since the two halves have the same essence, what is possible for one is possible for the other. Thus, if one half can touch the other with its first face, then the other half should be able to touch with its second face, implying that the object can separate or fragment. Therefore, any spatially located, extended entity is either a composite body or subject to division—both impossible for Allah. The argument concludes that Allah cannot be in a direction or space.

Key Terms
مشار إليه (mushār ilayh)
يمين العرش (yamīn al-‘arsh)
يسار العرش (yasār al-‘arsh)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Al-Razi conclude about any object that is 'great' and 'pointed to by sensory perception'?
A) It must be eternal.
B) It must have parts and limbs.
C) It must be indivisible.
D) It must be an accident.

Key Takeaway
Any spatially extended object must have distinct parts, otherwise contradictory directional attributes would apply.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God is not extended and has no parts, then He cannot be limited by space or time. Do you truly worship a Being beyond all spatial limitations, or do you unconsciously imagine Him in a location or direction? What would it take for your heart to fully embrace His transcendence?
?
Al-Razi's proof shows that any object with extension must have distinct parts, which leads to contradiction if considered one. Do you ever think of Allah as having 'sides' or 'directions'? This week, when you pray, consciously remind yourself that Allah is not confined to any direction. How does that change your focus and humility?
?
The argument uses a logical contradiction to establish a truth about God. Are you willing to let go of any anthropomorphic images you hold of God, even if they feel comforting? What is the cost of maintaining such images in your understanding of tawhid?

Parts Imply Divisibility
Al-Razi argues that parts lead to possible divisibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's argument that if an object has parts, then it is either composite or subject to division, both impossible for Allah.

Core Idea
Composite bodies can divide.

Having established that a spatially extended object must have parts, Al-Razi now considers two halves and argues that they could potentially separate. This shows that such an object is either composed of parts or subject to division—both impossible for the Necessary Being.

Guided Path
1
Read the second half of the passage
Read from 'وإذا ثبت هذا' to the end. This builds on the previous conclusion.
The argument uses symmetry of halves.
2
Understand the touching faces argument
Each half touches the other with one face. The faces are identical in essence, so what is possible for one is possible for the other.
3
Follow to the conclusion
Since one half can touch with its first face, the other must be able to touch with its second face, implying possible separation.
This leads to the final conclusion about composition and divisibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة : إن كل ما كان مشارا إليه بحب الحس ، وكان شيئا عظيما ، فإنه لا بد وأن نفرض فيه الأجزاء والأعضاء ، لأن الشيء الذي منه يحاذي يمين العرش ، غير الشيء الذي منه يحاذي يسار العرش ، وكيف لا نقول ذلك ونقول : بأن هذا الجانب يحاذي يمين العرش لا يساره ، والجانب الآخر منه يحاذي يسار العرش لا يمينه ؟ فلو كان الجانبان شيئا واحدا ، لزم اجتماع النفي والإثبات ، وأنه محال
وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : كل واحد من النصفين يماس النصف الآخر بأحد وجهيه دون الثاني . والوجهان متساويان في تمام الماهية ، والمتساويان في تمام الماهية ، يجب أن يصح على كل واحد منها ما يصح على الآخر ، وكما صح على أحد النصفين أن يماس النصف الآخر بأحد وجهيه دون الثاني ، وجب أن يصح عليه أن يماسه بالوجه الثاني دون الأول . ومتى صح ذلك ، لزم صحة التفرق والتمزق عليه ، فيثبت : أن كل ما حصل في الجهة والحيز ، وكان عظيم الذات ، فإنه يكون جسما مؤلفا من الأجزاء ، أو يكون التفرق والتمزق عليه
The ninth proof: Everything that is pointed to by sensory perception and is something great (magnitude), inevitably we must assume in it parts and limbs, because that from which it faces the right side of the Throne is other than that from which it faces the left side of the Throne. How could we not say that, and we say that this side faces the right of the Throne, not its left, and the other side faces the left of the Throne, not its right? So if the two sides were one thing, the conjunction of negation and affirmation would be necessary, and that is impossible. And when this is established, we say: Each of the two halves touches the other half with one of its two faces and not the other. And the two faces are equal in complete essence, and things equal in complete essence must have the same possibility as the other. Just as it is valid for one of the two halves to touch the other half with one of its two faces and not the other, so it must be valid for it to touch it with the second face and not the first. And whenever that is valid, the possibility of separation and fragmentation is necessary for it. Thus is established: Everything that occurs in direction and space and is great in essence must be a body composed of parts, or else separation and fragmentation are possible for it.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage presents the ninth argument (al-ḥujjah al-tāsi‘ah). It starts by considering a large object pointed to by sensory perception. Such an object must have parts because different parts face different directions—e.g., one side faces the right of the Throne, another the left. If both sides were identical, then contradictory attributions (facing right and not facing right) would apply, which is impossible. Then the argument considers two halves of such an object. أعضاء (a‘ḍā')
تماثل (tamāthul)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument claims that the object actually separates, not that separation is possible.
Correction: The argument only establishes the possibility of separation (صحة التفرق), not actual separation.

Checkpoint
What does the ninth argument conclude about anything that is in a direction and great in essence?
A) It must be a necessary being.

Key Takeaway
Spatially extended objects are either composite or divisible, both impossible for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Two Meanings of Place and Their Refutation
A second response to the argument about place, distinguishing two interpretations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how distinguishing two meanings of 'place' refutes the notion that God is in a location.

Core Idea
Place is not a single concept; two interpretations lead to different refutations.

In this passage, the author continues responding to an argument about God and place. He offers a second line of reasoning by clarifying that the term 'place' can mean two different things. By breaking down these meanings, he shows that either way, the claim that God occupies a place is untenable. This lesson will walk you through his distinction and logical conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once for overall flow, then the English translation. Notice the author's clear structure.
The author uses a conditional argument: 'if ... then'.
2
Identify the two definitions of 'place'
Locate the two interpretations: (1) dimension in which a body penetrates, (2) surrounding surface. These are mutually exclusive options.
The Arabic terms are 'بعد' and 'سطح محيط'.
3
Analyze the first option
If 'place' means dimension, the answer was already given in the first aspect. The author says it is a 'correct distinction' (فَرْق صحيح).
This refers back to a previous argument.
4
Analyze the second option
If 'place' means surrounding surface, the author argues that the entire world is not in a location or direction. It is a composite of parts.
This is a key premise: the universe itself is not 'in' anything.
5
Apply the reasoning to God
If you were to say God is in a place (as surrounding surface), it would imply He is a body composed of parts, which has been refuted earlier. Thus the argument fails.
The author concludes this view is false (باطل).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني في الجواب : أن نقول : المكان إما أن يكون مفسرا بالبعد الذي ينفذ فيه الجسم ، أو بالسطح المحيط . فإن كان الحق هو الأول فالجواب ما ذكرناه في الوجه الأول . وهو فرق صحيح ، وإن كان الحق هو الثاني ، قلنا : إن كل العالم ليس في حيز وجهة البتة ، بل هو ذات مركبة من الأجزاء والأبعاض، فإن حكمتم بكون الباري تعالى كذلك ، كان ذلك قولا بأنه جسم مؤلف من الأجزاء ، وقد سبق بيان أن ذلك قول باطل
The second aspect of the answer: that we say: 'place' is either interpreted as the dimension in which the body penetrates, or as the surrounding surface. If the truth is the first, then the answer is what we mentioned in the first aspect, and it is a correct distinction. And if the truth is the second, we say: the whole world is not in a location or direction at all, but is a composite essence of parts and limbs. If you judge that the Exalted Creator is likewise, that would be a statement that He is a body composed of parts, and it has preceded that this statement is false.

Commentary
This passage presents a second aspect of an answer regarding the concept of place (al-makan) and its relation to God. The author begins by specifying two interpretations of 'place': it can mean the dimension in which a body penetrates, or it can mean the surrounding surface. If the correct interpretation is the first, then the answer is as previously given in the first aspect, which is a valid distinction. If the correct interpretation is the second (the surrounding surface), then the author argues that the entire world (the physical universe) is not in any location or direction at all; it is a composite essence of parts and limbs. Therefore, if one were to apply that to God, it would imply that He is a body composed of parts, which has already been refuted. Thus, this argument refutes the idea that God can be in a place.

Eighth Proof: The Logic of Sensory Indication
A logical proof that sensory indication implies body or accident, so God is not in a direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proof that anything that can be pointed to by the senses must be either a body or an accident, and therefore God, being neither, transcends all directions.

Core Idea
Sensory location necessarily implies either a body or an accident.

This lesson presents the eighth proof from the author's series on divine transcendence. The proof uses a logical division (dichotomy) to show that anything that can be perceived as being 'here' or 'there' falls into one of two categories: body or accident. Since God is neither, He cannot be in any direction or place. This is a concise and powerful argument grounded in the nature of sensory perception.

Guided Path
1
Understand the logical division
The proof begins by dividing all things that can be pointed to into two kinds: those indicated primarily/independently (bodies) and those indicated secondarily/dependently (accidents).
This division is exhaustive for sensory indication.
2
Apply the division to God
The author then reminds us that it has already been shown that God is not a body, and He cannot be an accident because accidents require a substrate.
The previous chapter established that God is not a body.
3
Draw the conclusion
Therefore, since neither category applies, God is not located in any place or direction.
This conclusion is the desired proof of transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثامنة : إن كل ما صحت الإشارة الحسية إليه بأنه ههنا أو هناك ، فإما أن يكون موصوفا بهذه الصفة على سبيل الأصالة والاستقلال ، أو على سبيل التبعية ، فإن كان الأول فهو الجسم ، وإن كان الثاني فهو العرض ، ولما دللنا في الفصل المتقدم على أنه يمتنع كونه جسما . وظاهر أنه أيضا ليس بعرض ، وإلا لكان محتاجا إلى المحل ، فحينئذ يلزم منه امتناع كونه حاصلا في الحيز والجهة . وهو المطلوب
The eighth proof: Everything to which sensory indication is valid as 'here' or 'there' is either characterized by this attribute in a primary and independent manner, or in a secondary manner. If the first, then it is a body; if the second, then it is an accident. Since we have demonstrated in the previous chapter that it is impossible for Him to be a body, and it is apparent that He is also not an accident, otherwise He would need a substrate; therefore, it follows that it is impossible for Him to be located in a place and direction. And that is what was sought.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is the eighth proof against God being in a direction or location. It is based on a logical division: anything that can be pointed to by the senses as being here or there must fall into one of two categories. If the indication is primary and independent, the object is a body (جسم). If it is secondary and dependent, the object is an accident (عرض). The author then notes that it has already been established that God cannot be a body (from previous arguments), and it is also clear that He cannot be an accident because an accident requires a substrate (محل) to inhere in. Therefore, since neither category applies to God, He cannot be located in any direction or place (حيز وجهة). This is a straightforward syllogism: sensory location implies body or accident; God is neither; therefore God is not in a location.

Correction: The proof shows that such pointing necessarily implies either body or accident, so it cannot apply to God.

Key Takeaway
God transcends all spatial and directional attributes because He is neither a body nor an accident.

Ninth Proof: Parts and Divisibility from Sensory Indication
Proof that sensory objects have parts, hence God is beyond direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that anything sensorily indicated and great must have parts, and why this establishes God's transcendence above direction and place.

Core Idea
Anything pointed to by the senses must have parts, so God cannot be in a place.

This proof builds on previous arguments by considering objects that are great in size and perceptible to the senses. It demonstrates that such objects necessarily have parts and are subject to divisibility, which is impossible for the Necessary Being. The argument uses subtle reasoning about sides, faces, and quiddity to show that direction implies composition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the argument's structure emerge naturally.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the initial premise
Notice the claim: anything sensorily indicated and great must have parts because different sides face different directions (right and left of the Throne). This is the foundation.
Why must distinct sides imply distinct parts? The author uses a contradiction argument.
3
Follow the analogy of halves and faces
The argument moves to two halves touching each other with one face. Because the faces are equal in quiddity, both faces are equally capable of touching, implying potential separation.
This step uses the principle of 'equality in quiddity' to generalize.
4
Understand the conclusion
The proof concludes: anything in a direction and place is either a composite body or subject to separation and disintegration. Since this is impossible for God, He is beyond direction and place.
This directly supports God's transcendence (tanzih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة التاسعة : إن كل ما كان مشارا إليه بالحس ، وكان شيئا عظيما ، فإنه لا بد وأن نفرض فيه الأجزاء والأعضاء ، لأن الشيء الذي منه يحاذي يمين العرش ، غير الشيء الذي منه يحاذي يسار العرش ، وكيف لا نقول ذلك ونقول : بأن هذا الجانب يحاذي يمين العرش لا يساره ، والجانب الآخر منه يحاذي يسار العرش لا يمينه ؟ فلو كان الجانبان شيئا واحدا ، لزم اجتماع النفي والإثبات ، وأنه محال . وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : كل واحد من النصفين يماس النصف الآخر بأحد وجهيه دون الثاني . والوجهان متساويان في تمام الماهية ، والمتساويان في تمام الماهية ، يجب أن يصح على كل واحد منها ما يصح على الآخر ، وكما صح على أحد النصفين أن يماس النصف الآخر بأحد وجهيه دون الثاني ، وجب أن يصح عليه أن يماسه بالوجه الثاني دون الأول . ومتى صح ذلك ، لزم صحة التفرق والتمزق عليه ، فيثبت : أن كل ما حصل في الجهة والحيز ، وكان عظيم الذات ، فإنه يكون جسما مؤلفا من الأجزاء ، أو يكون التفرق والتمزق عليه جائزا ، ولما كان ذلك على الله محال ، وجب القول بتنزيهة عن الحيز والجهة [ والله أعلم (۱) ] .
The ninth proof: Everything that is pointed to by sense perception and is something great, necessarily we assume in it parts and limbs, because that which from it faces the right of the Throne is other than that which from it faces the left of the Throne. How could we not say that, and say that this side faces the right of the Throne, not its left, and the other side from it faces the left of the Throne, not its right? If the two sides were one thing, then the conjunction of negation and affirmation would be necessary, and that is impossible. When this is established, we say: each of the two halves touches the other half with one of its two faces and not the second. The two faces are equal in complete quiddity. And things equal in complete quiddity must have what is valid for one valid for the other. Just as it is valid for one half to touch the other half with one of its faces and not the second, it must be valid for it to touch it with the second face and not the first. When that is valid, the validity of separation and disintegration upon it follows. Thus it is established: that everything that occurs in a direction and place and is great in essence is either a body composed of parts, or separation and disintegration are possible upon it. Since that is impossible for God, it is necessary to pronounce His transcendence above place and direction. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is the ninth proof, which argues from the concept of a great object (عظيم الذات) that can be pointed to by the senses. The author reasons that any such object must have parts, because when facing the Throne (العرش), different sides of the object face different directions (right and left). If the object had no parts, it would have to be both right and left simultaneously, a contradiction. Then, through a detailed argument about two halves touching each other with one face but not the other, and the equivalence of faces in quiddity (الماهية), the author shows that this object would be subject to possible separation (تفرق) and disintegration (تمزق) because each half could potentially touch the other with either face. Since this cannot apply to God, He cannot be in direction or place. The proof establishes that anything in a place is either composite (body) or divisible, both impossible for God.

أجزاء وأعضاء
محاذاة
يمين العرش
يسار العرش
نصفين
مماسة
وجهيه
ماهية
تفرق
تمزق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that facing different directions does not necessitate distinct parts.
Correction: The author argues that if the two sides were one, they would have to be both right and left simultaneously, which is a contradiction. Hence distinct parts are necessary.

Checkpoint
What does the ninth proof conclude about anything that is in a direction and is great in essence?
A) It must be eternal.
B) It must be either a body or subject to separation.
C) It must be an accident.
D) It must be simple.

Key Takeaway
The ninth proof establishes that direction implies composition and divisibility, so God, being indivisible, cannot be in a direction or place.
